рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

So far we had the section dealing with the Initiatory Ceremony. All that has been said here pertains to that ceremony.

тАЬWell, if so, then the Ke┼Ы─Бnta (spoken of in 65) would also pertain to the Initiation.тАЭ

Not so, as that sacrament has been laid down as to be performed at its own time, which comes long after the

Initiatory Ceremony has been finished. So that, even though it is mentioned in the same context, it becomes connected with other rites by virtue of the force of syntactical connection. Thus it is that some people regard the Ke┼Ы─Бnta as to be done after the Final Bath (to say nothing of the Initiation).

The term тАШaupan─БyanikaтАЩ means pertaining to the Upa nayana, the initial vowel being prolonged, as in other cases explained before.

тАШBirthтАЩтАФbeing born from their parents; this is what is тАШmarkedтАЩтАФmanifested, perfectedтАФby the said ceremony; even though born, the boy, before Initiation, is as good as not born; as till then he is not entitled to any religious acts. Hence the ceremony is what тАШmarksтАЩ his birth.

тАШSanctifiesтАЩтАФthis has been already explained.

The duties with which the initiated boy becomes connectedтАФto which he becomes entitled,тАФthose that should be performed by the initiated bovтАФall these are going to be expounded;тАФthese тАШnow learnтАЩтАФ(68)

Gautama-Dharmas┼лtra, 1.10.тАФтАШThe Upanayana is the second birth for the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa.тАЩ

Having initiated the pupil, the Teacher should, first of all, teach him cleanliness, right behaviour, firetending and also the twilight-devotions.тАФ(69)

рдЕрдзреНрдпрдпрдирдзрд░реНрдорд╛рдиреН рдЗрджрд╛рдиреАрдореН рдЖрд╣ ред

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШShould teachтАЩтАФshould make him learn.

тАШFirst of allтАЩ;тАФthis does not mean that Cleanliness should be taught before Right Behaviour and the rest; in fact, there is no order of sequence intended among those mentioned here; all that the text is going to lay down is that after the Initiation there should he the teaching of the observances; and after the pupil has been instructed regarding the observances, he should proceed with the study of the Veda. Hence if the text meant that the boy should be taught Fire-kindling and the Twilight-Devotions before being taught the observances, it would be laying down for him the reciting of mantras not prescribed anywhere else,тАФbecause each of the two acts mentioned is performed with mantras. As for тАШcleanliness,тАЩ there can be no fixed time for it; and it must be taught on the very day on which the boy has been initiated. So also тАШRight Behaviour.тАЩ For these reasons it is clear that the phrase тАШfirst of allтАЩ is meant to denote importance, and it does not mean that it is to be taught before everything else.

тАШCleanlinessтАЩтАФstands for all those acts that begin with the washing of the private parts, once, &c., &c. (5. 136) and ending with the sipping of water.

тАШRight BehaviourтАЩтАФrising to receive the Teacher and other superiors, offering them seat and saluting them.

тАШFire-tendingтАЩтАФthe kindling of fire, and supplying of fuel.

The devotion offered at twiligh, to the Sun, consists in meditating upon the form of the Sun. This is what is meant by the тАШTwilight-Devotions.тАЩ Or, it may refer to what is going to be prescribed below, in verse 101.

This is what constitutes the тАШDuty relating to Observances.тАЩтАФ(69)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

This verse is quoted in Vidh─Бnap─Бrij─Бta (p. 491).

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рддреБрд▓реНрдп-рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐

Y─Бj├▒avalkya, 1.15.тАФтАШThe Teacher, having initiated the pupil, should teach him the Mah─Бvy─Бhс╣Ыtis and the Veda, and then instruct him regarding cleanliness and practices.тАЩ

─А┼Ыval─Бyana-Gс╣Ыhyas┼лtra, 22.1.тАФтАШHaving tied the girdle-zone and handed over the staff, he should instruct him regarding the duties of studentship, addressing him thus;тАФтАЬThou art a religious student, sip water, do your duty, sleep not during the day, under the guidance of your teacher study the Veda.тАЭ

Gautama-Dharmas┼лtra, 1.12; 3.5.тАФтАШHe is a Teacher, because he expounds the Veda;тАФthe student should remain under the Teacher.тАЩ

─Аpastamba-Dharmas┼лtra, 1.1.9, 12, 14.тАФтАШUpanayana is the Vedic sacrament, for one who is seeking after knowledge; for that purpose one should seek an initiator who would belong to a noble family and be endowed with learning and self-control,тАФand under him one should remain till the completion of his study;тАФhe is called ─Аcarya because be contributes to the accumulation (─Бcinoti) of Dharma.тАЩ

Artha┼Ы─Бstra (p. 30).тАФтАШFor the student, Vedic study, Fire-feeding, Bathing, Living on alms, Attending on the Teacher till death, and in his absence, on his son or on a fellow-student.тАЩ

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

The Future ending (in тАШadhy─лс╣гyam─Бс╣Зaс╕етАЩ) denotes the immediate future; and means тАШwhen engaging in study,тАЩ тАШwhen beginning to study,тАЩ тАШwhen desiring to proceed with his study.тАЩ

тАШHe shall be taught, with hist face to the north.тАЩтАФGautama (1.65) has laid down that тАШthe pupil should face the east, while the Teacher faces the west.тАЩ

тАШWhen he has sipped water according to lawтАЩтАФrefers to the rules prescribed above regarding the sipping of water.

The compound тАШbrahm─Б├▒jalikс╣Ыtaс╕етАЩ is to be expounded as тАШhe by whom Brahm─Б├▒jali has been formed.тАЩ the past participal adjective (тАШkс╣Ыtaс╕етАЩ)being placed at the end, according to P─Бс╣Зini 2.2.37;тАФthe present compound being analogous to such compounds as тАШ─Бhit─БgniтАЩ and the like. Or, we may read тАШbrahm─Б├▒jalikс╣Ыt.тАЩ

тАШWears light clothingтАЩ;тАФi.e., with clothes thoroughly washed; a thorough washing always makes the cloth тАШlightтАЩ; hence тАШlightnessтАЩ indicates cleanliness. Or, тАШlight clothingтАЩ may be taken in its literal sense, the lightness of the clothing being meant to serve a visible purpose: if the boy were

Heavily clad in thick woolen clothes, he would not feel the strokes of the rope with which he would be struck when found to be inattentive, and not feeling the stroke, he would not study in the proper manner; and if the teacher, on this account, found it necessary to remove the cloth from the back (each time that the rope would be laid on the back), this would tire the teacher himself; and further, if the boy were struck with the rope on the naked body, he, would feel great pain.

тАШOne who has his organs under full controlтАЩ;тАФi.e., one who has fully subdued all bis organs, both external and internal. The sense is that he should not turn his eyes this way and that, should not listen to anything and everything that may be talked of, he should devote all his attention to his own study.тАФ(70)

тАШLaghuv─Бs─Бс╕етАЩтАФLightly cothed,тАФclothed with washed, and hence light, dressтАЩ (Medh─Бtithi);тАФтАШwith clean clothes (Kull┼лka);тАФтАШclothed in dress which is not gorgeous, i. e. which is less valuable than the TeacherтАЩsтАЩ (R─Бghav─Бnanda).

Burnell refers to Ch. XV of Pr─Бti┼Ы─Бkhya of the с╣Ъgveda.

K─Бmandaka (2. 22-23).тАФтАШThe duties of the Religious Student areтАФto live in the house of his preceptor, to tend the sacred fires, to study the Veda and its auxiliaries, to observe vows, to perform ablutions three times, to beg alms, and live with the teacher all his life In the absence of the preceptor, he may live with the preceptorтАЩs son, or with one of his fellow-students;тАФor if he likes, he may adopt another mode of life.тАЩ

  • рд╕рдВрд╣рддреНрдп рд╕рдВрд▓рдЧреНрдиреМ рд╕рдВрд╢реНрд▓рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреМ рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░рдВ рдХреГрддреНрд╡рд╛ рдЕрдзреНрдпреЗрдпрдореН ред рдХрдЪреНрдЫрдк8 рдЗрддрд┐ рдпрдГ рд╕рдВрдирд┐рд╡реЗрд╢реЛ рд╣рд╕реНрддрдпреЛрдГ рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрд╕реН рддрдерд╛ рдХрд░реНрддрд╡реНрдпрдГ ред рд╕ рд╣рд┐ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдорд╛рдЮреНрдЬрд▓рд┐рдГ ред рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердХрдердирдореН рдПрддрддреН рее реи.ренрез рее
рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

Though the term тАШbrahmaтАЩ has many meanings, yet, in view of the fact of the present context bearing on тАШstudy,тАЩ it is taken here as standing for the Veda.

тАШAt the beginning of the VedaтАЩ;тАФthe Locative ending denotes occasion; and since the context bears upon тАШstudy,тАЩ the beginning meant is that of the action of study; and the тАШbeginningтАЩ stands for the very first recitation by the person concerned. And it is at this first recitation that the TeacherтАЩs feet are to be clasped. The term тАШbeginningтАЩ here cannot stand for the first letters of the VedasтАФтАШagnim─лleтАЩ (с╣Ъgveda), тАШikhe tvorjeтАЩ (Yajurveda), тАШagna ─Бy─БhiтАЩ (S─Бmaveda); because these opening words could never form the occasion (for the clasping of the feet); for the simple reason that (being parts of the eternal Veda) they are ever present; while it is only what is itself occasional (occurring only at certain times) that can be the occasion for anything. Hence what is meant is thatтАФтАШwhen one is going to begin the study of the Veda, he should clasp the TeacherтАЩs feet, and having done that he should recite the words of the Veda and it does not mean that he should clasp the TeacherтАЩs feet every time that he may study the Veda.

тАЬThe first moment of the act is what is called its тАШbeginningтАЩ; and it is this beginning that is spoken of as the occasion. Now it is only what is existent that can form the occasion for anything; e.g., when living existence is regarded as the occasion for the performance of Agnihotra, it is the existence that is present. It is true that in some cases, the burning of the house and such other past events also are spoken of as the occasion for certain acts; but in these cases we accept them as such because that is what is actually prescribed. In the present instance however, the тАШbeginning of studyтАЩ and тАШclasping of the feetтАЩ should be regarded as simultaneous.тАЭ

Our answer to the above is as follows:тАФWhat is called тАШbeginningтАЩ here is the making up of oneтАЩs mind to study, and not the first moment of the act. The Boy makes up his mind to study as soon as the Teacher addresses to him the words тАШnow readтАЩ; so that it is after this that the feet are to be clasped. This is intended to be the propitiation of the Teacher who is going to bestow a favour. Just as in the ordinary world, when a person is going to bestow a favour upon another, the latte? welcomes him with the wordsтАФтАШit is through you that I have been saved from this sin.тАЩ

This clasping of the feet is meant to embody the speechless requestтАФтАШwe are ready to proceed with our studyтАЩ; for the Teacher is never to be directed with the words тАШnow teach us.тАЩ All that is to be done is that the Boy should approach him (and clasp his feet), with a view to remind him that it is time for study, and it is only after this approaching has been done, that the words of the Veda should begin to he recited.

Further, in view of the rule that тАШone should study the Veda with joined palms,тАЩ if the boy were to study (with joined palms), he would he transgressing the rule regarding the damping of feet (if the study and the were meant to he simultaneous) [for one who would have his hands joined could not clasp the feet].

тАШfindтАЩтАФCeasing, desisting from study.

Though the term тАШbrahmaтАЩ is the subordinate factor in the compound (тАШbrahm─БrambheтАЩ) yet, in as much as the term тАШendтАЩ is a relative term, it is taken as correlated to the term тАШbrahmaтАЩ; specially because there is no other word in the text with which it could be connected.

тАШAlwaysтАЩтАФimplies that this rule regarding the clasping of feet should he observed at the beginning and end of all future study, every day. If this word were not present, the rule would be taken as applying to only that тАШbeginning of studyтАЩ which comes immediately after the Initiatory Ceremony; on the analogy of the ─Аrambhaс╣З─лy─Б Iс╣гс╣нi, which is performed only at the beginning of the first sacrifice performed by the Agnihotrin, after he has done the тАШFire-kindling,тАЩ and not at that of each succeeding p┼лrnam─Бsa, which is performed every month.

From morning till such time as the daily routine of reciting two Chapters has not been finished, the whole is regarded as a single act of тАШstudyтАЩ; so that if at intervals, there is some obstruction, the resuming of study on the same day is not regarded as тАШbeginningтАЩ; and at each resumption, the feet are not clasped. In another Smс╣Ыti we readтАФтАШThe clasping of the TeacherтАЩs feet should be done every day in the morning.тАЩ Gautama, 2.53).

тАШHaving joinedтАЩтАФmaking them touch one another.

тАШShould be studiedтАЩ;тАФwhat is meant is that the hands should he placed in that posture which resembles the tortoise.

тАШThis is Brahm─Б├▒jaliтАЩ;тАФthis explains the meaning of the term тАШbrahm─Б├▒jaliтАЩтАФ(71)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

The first half of this verse is quoted in V─лramitrodaya (.Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 532) where Sad─Б is explained as everyday at the time of study, and тАШp─Бda-grahaс╣ЗamтАЩ as saluting-тАФand the second half is quoted on p. 524, as containing the definition of the тАШBrahm─Б├▒jaliтАЩ;тАФand in Smс╣Ыticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 136).

071 At the beginning and at the end of (a lesson in the) Veda he must always clasp both the feet of his teacher, (and) he must study, joining his hands; that is called the Brahmangali (joining the palms for the sake of the Veda).

The clasping op the teacherтАЩs feet should be done with crossed hands: the left should be touched with the left and the right with the right.тАФ(72)

рдпрджреН рдЙрдкрд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╣рдгрдВ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╢реНрд▓реЛрдХреЗ рдЧреБрд░реЛрд░реН рдЙрдХреНрддрдВ рддрджреН рд╡реНрдпрддреНрдпрд╕реНрддрдкрд╛рдгрд┐рдирд╛ рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпрдореН ред рдХреАрджреГрд╢рдГ рдкреБрдирдГ рдкрд╛рдгреНрдпреЛрд░реН рд╡реНрдпрддреНрдпрд╛рд╕рдГ рдХрд░реНрддрд╡реНрдп рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЕрдд рдЖрд╣ ред рд╕рд╡реНрдпреЗрди рд╣рд╕реНрддреЗрди рд╕рд╡реНрдпрдГ рдкрд╛рджрдГ рд╕реНрдкреНрд░рд╖реНрдЯрд╡реНрдпрдГ рд╕реНрдкрд░реНрд╢рдГ рдХрд░реНрддрд╡реНрдпрдГ, рди рддреБ рдЪрд┐рд░рдВ рдирд┐рдкреАрдбреНрдпрд╛рд╕рд┐рддрд╡реНрдпрдореН ред рдПрд╖ рдЪ рд╡реНрдпрддреНрдпрд╛рд╕реЛ рдпреБрдЧрдкрджреН рдЗрддрд░реЗрддрд░рджрд┐рдХреНрд╕рдВрдЪрд╛рд░реЗрдг рд╣рд╕реНрддрдпреЛрд░реН рднрд╡рддрд┐ ред рдЕрдЧреНрд░рддрдГ рд╕реНрдерд┐рддреЗрди рд╕рдВрдореБрдЦреЗрди рдЧреБрд░реЛрд░реН рдЙрдкрд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╣рдгрдВ рдХрд░реНрддрд╡реНрдпрдореН ред рддрддреНрд░ рд╡рд╛рдореЛ рджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгрдорд╛рд░реНрдЧрдВ рдиреАрдпрддреЗ, рджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгреЛ рд╡рд╛рдордореН рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдПрд╡рдВ рд╕рд╡реНрдпреЗрди рд╕рд╡реНрдпрдГ рд╕реНрдкреГрд╖реНрдЯреЛ рднрд╡рддрд┐, рджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгреЗрди рдЪ рджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдг рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдПрд╖ рдкрд╛рдгрд┐рд╡реНрдпрддреНрдпрд╛рд╕рдГ ред

  • рдЕрдиреНрдпреЗ рддреБ “рд╡рд┐рдиреНрдпрд╕реНрддрдкрд╛рдгрд┐рдирд╛” рдЗрддрд┐ рдкрдардиреНрддрд┐ ред рд╕реНрдкрд░реНрд╢рд╛рджреН рдПрд╡ рдЪ рд╡рд┐рдиреНрдпрд╛рд╕реЗ рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзреЗ рдирд╛рдЧреНрдирд┐рддрдкреНрддрд╛рдпрдГрдкрд┐рдгреНрдбрд╕реНрдкрд░реНрд╢рдирд╡рджреН рджрд╛рд╣рднрдпрд╛рджреН рдЕрдЩреНрдЧреБрд▓реНрдпрдЧреНрд░рдорд╛рддреНрд░реЗрдг рд╕реНрдкрд░реНрд╢рдирдВ рди9 рдХрд░реНрддрд╡реНрдпрдореН, рдЕрдкрд┐ рддреБ рд╣рд╕реНрддреМ рд╡рд┐рдиреНрдпрд╕рд┐рддрд╡реНрдпреМ рдирд┐рдзрд╛рддрд╡реНрдпреМ ред рдкреАрдбрдирдВ рддреБ рдкреАрдбрд╛рдХрд░рдВ рдирд┐рд╖рд┐рджреНрдзрдореН рдЗрддрд┐ рд╡рд░реНрдгрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рее реи.ренреи рее
рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

The тАШclasping of the TeacherтАЩs feetтАЩ mentioned in the preceding verse тАШshould be done with crossed hands.тАЩ

In answer to the question as to what sort of the тАШcrossingтАЩ of hands should be done, the Author addsтАФтАШthe leftтАЩ foot тАШshould be touched with the leftтАЩ hand; it is mere touching that should be done, the Teacher should not be troubled by the foot being held for a long time. This тАШcrossingтАЩ is obtained by the two hands being simultaneously moved towards one another. That is, the feet having to be clasped by the pupil standing in front of the Teacher; the left hand is moved towards the right and the right towards the left; it is thus that the left foot becomes touched by the left hand and the right foot by the right hand. This is the тАШcrossing of the hands.тАЩ

Others read the text as тАШvinyastap─Бс╣Зin─Б,тАЩ тАШwith well-placed hands.тАЩ The тАШplacingтАЩ being implied by the touching, what the addition of the epithet would imply is that the feet should not be touched merely with the finger tips,тАФin the way in which a red-hot piece of iron is touched, for fear of burning,тАФbut the hands should be тАШwell-plaed,тАЩ actually held upon the feet. Pressing of the feet would cause pain to the Teacher, and is as such prohibited. Such is the explanation provided of this version of the text.тАФ(72)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

This verse is quoted in V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 455), where it is explained that the тАШleftтАЩ and тАШrightтАЩ of the second half stand for the left and right feet; so that the meaning is that the left foot of the teacher should be touched by the left hand and the right one by the right hand; and it quotes Baudh─Бyann laying down that the pupil should pass his hands from the knee downwards to the foot.

A similar explanation is given also in Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava (─Аc─Бra, p. 300).

The verse is quoted also in Vidh─Бnap─Бrij─Бta (p. 52.1);тАФin Apar─Бrka (p. 55), as laying down the тАШfeet claspingтАЩ of the teacher;тАФin Saс╣Гsk─Бramay┼лkha (p. 40), which says that тАШspraс╣гс╣нavyaс╕етАЩ goes with тАШgurucaraс╣Зaс╕етАЩ understood;тАФand in Smс╣Ыticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 103), which explains the meaning to be that the left and right feet of the teacher are to be touched with the left and right hands respectively.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рддреБрд▓реНрдп-рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐

Gautama-Dharmas┼лtra, 1. 58.тАФтАШThe clasping of the teacherтАЩs feet.тАЩ

Gautama-Dharmas┼лtra, 6. 1.тАФтАШEvery day on meeting, the feet of the teacher should be clasped.тАЩ

Gautama-Dharmas┼лtra (Apar─Бrka, p. 55).тАФтАШAlso daily in the morning, as well as at the beginning and end of Vedic lectures.тАЩ

─Аpastamba-Dharmas┼лtra, 1.2.5.21-22.тАФтАШWith the right hand clasping the right foot, he should touch it both up and down, along with the ankle;тАФaccording to others, the two feet should he clasped with the two hands.тАЩ

─Аpastamba (Apar─Бrka, p. 55).тАФтАШAt sunrise, he shall meet the teacher and clasp his feet.тАЩ

Baudh─Бyana-Dharmas┼лtra, 1. 2. 26.тАФтАШClasping the right foot with the right, and the left with the left hand, one obtains long life and goes to heaven.тАЩ

Paith─лnasi (V─лramitrodaya-Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 455).тАФтАШWith the palms of the two hands turned upwards, he should clasp the two feet of the teacher, the right with the right and the left with the left.тАЩ

Va┼Ыiс╣гс╣нha (V─лramitrodaya-Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. V56).тАФтАШThe clasping of the teacherтАЩs feet should be done.тАЩ

Baudh─Бyana (Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava, p. 300).тАФтАШTouching his ears, concentrating his mind, he shall touch the teacher below his knees down to his feet, this is feet-clasping.тАЩ

Atri (Apar─Бrka, p. 55).тАФтАШOrdinarily one should salute by raising the right band; hands should be joined in saluting a Vedic scholar; in the case of the teacher, the feet should he clasped.тАЩ

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдореВрд▓рд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

When the pupil is going to study, the Teacher, ever free from indolence, should sayтАФтАШho, read!тАЩ and he should cease when he says тАШlet there be a stop!тАЩтАФ(73).

рдореЗрдзрд╛рддрд┐рдерд┐рдГ

рдЕрдзреНрдпреЗрд╖реНрдпрдорд╛рдгрдореН рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджреАрдирд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдЧреНрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдЦреНрдпрд╛рддрд╛рдирд┐ рдкрджрд╛рдирд┐ ред рдЧреБрд░реЛрд░реН рдЕрдпрдВ рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧрдГ ред рдЧреБрд░реЛрд░реН рдпрджрд╛ рдорд╛рдгрд╡рдХреЛ рд╜рдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдпрд┐рддреБрдореН рдЕрднрд┐рд▓рд╖рд┐рддрд╕реН рддрджрд╛ рдЕрдзреАрд╖реНрд╡ рднреЛ рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЖрдордиреНрддреНрд░рдпрд┐рддрд╡реНрдпрдГ ред рдЕрдирд╛рдордиреНрддреНрд░рд┐рддреЗрди рди рдЧреБрд░реБрдГ рдЦреЗрджрдпрд┐рддрд╡реНрдпрдГ “рдЙрдкрджрд┐рд╢рд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рдХрдореН” рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдЙрдХреНрддрдВ рдЪ ред “рдЖрд╣реВрддрд╢реН рдЪрд╛рдкреНрдпреН рдЕрдзреАрдпреАрдд” (рдпреНрдзреН рез.реирен) рдЗрддрд┐ ред рд╡рд┐рд░рд╛рдореЛ рд╜рд╕реНрддреНрд╡реН рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдПрддрдВ рд╢рдмреНрджрдВ рд╕рдореБрдЪреНрдЪрд╛рд░реНрдпреНрдЖрд░рдореЗрддреН рдирд┐рд╡рд░реНрддреЗрдд ред рдХрдГ ред рдЧреБрд░реБрд░реН рдПрд╡, рдкреНрд░рдердорд╛рдиреНрддрдирд┐рд░реНрджреЗрд╢рд╛рддреН ред рдЕрде рд╡рд╛ рдЧреБрд░реБрдгреЛрддреНрд╕реГрд╖реНрдЯреЛ рдирд┐рд╡рд░реНрддреЗрдд, рди рд╕реНрд╡реЗрдЪреНрдЫрдпрд╛ ред рдПрд╡рдВ рдЪреИрддрджреН рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдЦреНрдпрд╛рдпрддреЗ-10 “рдпрджрд╛ рдЧреБрд░реБрд░реН рд╡рд┐рд░рд╛рдореЛ рд╜рд╕реНрддреНрд╡реН рдЗрддрд┐ рдмреНрд░реВрдпрд╛рддреН, рддрджрд╛ рд╡рд┐рд░рдореЗрджреН рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордЪрд╛рд░реА” ред

  • рдЕрдиреНрдпреЗ рддреНрд╡реН рдЕрдзреНрдпреЗрддреГрдорд╛рддреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдгрд╛рдореН рдЙрдкрд╛рдзреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╕реНрдп рдЪ рдЙрдкрд░рдордгрдХрд╛рд▓реЗ рдзрд░реНрдордореН рдЗрдордореН рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрд┐ ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪ рд╕реНрдореГрддреНрдпрдиреНрддрд░рдореН- “рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдзреНрдпрд╛рдпрдореН рдЕрдзреАрддреНрдп рд╡рд┐рд░рдордгрдХрд╛рд▓реЗ рдкреНрд░рджреЗрд╢рд┐рдиреНрдпрд╛ рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реАрдореН рдЖрд▓рднреНрдп рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрддреАрддрд┐ рдпрдЬреБрдГрд╖реБ11 рдмреНрд░реВрдпрд╛рддреН, рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрдкрд╖реНрдЯрдореН12 рдЗрддрд┐ рд╕рд╛рдорд╕реБ, рд╡рд┐рд░рд╛рдордГ рдкрд░рдорд╛рд╕реНрд╡реН рдЛрдХреНрд╖реБ, рдЖрд░рдорд╕реН рддреНрд╡реН рдЕрдерд░реНрд╡рд╕реБ” ред

рдЕрддрдиреНрджреНрд░рд┐рдд рдЕрдирд▓рд╕рдГ ред рддрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рд▓рд╕реНрдпрдореН ред рддрджреНрдпреЛрдЧрд╛рддреН рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╕реН рддрдиреНрджреНрд░рд┐рдд рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЙрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рддреНрдпрдХреНрддреНрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╕реНрдпрдореН рдЕрддрдиреНрджреНрд░рд┐рддрдГ ред рдЕрдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрд╢реН рдЪрд╛рдпрдореН ред рдирд╛рддреНрд░ рддрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛ рд╢реНрд░рдордГ ред рди рддреНрд╡реН рдЗрдпрдореН рдЖрд╢рдЩреНрдХрд╛ рдХрд░реНрддрд╡реНрдпрд╛- “рдп рдЕрддрдиреНрджреНрд░рд┐рддрд╕реН рддрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдпрдВ рд╡рд┐рдзрд┐рдГ, рдЖрд▓рд╕реНрдпрд╡рддрд╕реН рддреНрд╡реН рдЕрдиреНрдпрдГ” рее реи.ренрей рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШWhen going to studyтАЩ and the other expressions have already been explained before. The present verse adds a direction for the Teacher. When a boy is desirous to read the Veda from a Teacher, he should be invited with the words тАШho, read!тАЩ Until he is so invited, the Boy should not press the Teacher with such importunate requests asтАФтАШplease teach us this chapter!тАЩ Another Smс╣Ыti has declaredтАФтАШOne should study on being invited to do soтАЩ. (Y─Бj├▒avalkya, ─Аc─Бra, 27).

Saying the words тАШlet there be a stop,тАЩ тАШhe should ceaseтАЩтАФdesist,тАФтАШwho is to cease?тАЩтАФThe Teacher; as is clear from the nominative case-ending used. Or, it may be taken to mean that the pupil should cease only when dismissed by the Teacher, and not according to his own wish; the construction of the passage in this case beingтАФтАШwhen the Teacher says let there be a stop, then the pupil should cease.тАЩ

Other people have explained this rule regarding the time of ceasing as applying to all readersтАФthe pupil as well as the Teacher. And this is in accordance with another Smс╣Ыti, which saysтАФтАЬHaving recited the Veda, at the time of ceasing, one should touch the ground with the fore-finger and pronounce тАШsvastiтАЩ in the case of the Yajurveda, тАШvispaс╣гс╣н─БmтАЩ in the case of the S─Бman, тАШvir─Бmaс╕етАЩ in the case of the с╣Ъgveda and тАШ─БramasvaтАЩ in the case of the Atharva.тАЭ

тАШFree from indolenceтАЩтАФwithout sloth; тАШindolenceтАЩ is sloth;тАФthe man beset with sloth is called тАШindolentтАЩ; and when he has given it up he is called тАШfrom indolence.тАЩ This is meant to be merely descriptive. тАШIndolenceтАЩ here does not mean fatigue. The present text should never be taken to mean that what is here laid down is for only one who is free from indolence, while for those beset with indolence there is some other rule.тАФ(73)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa and Nandana read тАШadhyeс╣гyam─Бс╣Зastu gurum etc,тАЩ which meansтАФтАШthe pupil, proceeding to study, shall say to his Teacher etc., etc.тАЩ

This verse is quoted in Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava (─Аc─Бra, p. 136), where the verse is explained to mean thatтАФтАШeach day at the beginning of the teaching, the Teacher should begin the work with the word тАШHo! read;тАЩ and at the end, should finish with the words тАШLet there he a stop;тАЩ and it adds that all this is to be done for the purpose of тАШpleasing God.тАЩ

The verse is quoted also in Madanap─Бrij─Бta (p. 100);тАФin Vidh─Бnap─Бrij─Бta (p. 521);тАФin V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 514);тАФin Saс╣Гsk─Бramay┼лkha (p. 52);тАФand in Smс╣Ыticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 142), which explains ─Бrame as тАШshould desist from teaching.тАЩ

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рддреБрд▓реНрдп-рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐

Gautama- Dharmas┼лtra, 1. 52.тАФтАШClasping the left, foot with his hand, he should address the request to himтАФpray read.тАЩ

─Аpastamba-Dharmas┼лtra, 1.3.10,13,15.тАФтАШWhen one desirous of learning meets a learned man, he should obtain his permission and then proceed to read; and having approached near the teacher, he should read after having requested the teacher to please read.тАЩ

Yama (V─лramitrodaya-Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 514).тАФтАШRegularly rising in the morning, he should cleanse his teeth, bathe, pour libations into fire; then the man should carry on teaching.тАЩ

─Аpastamba (V─лramitrodaya-Saс╣Гsk─Бra).тАФтАШOne should avoid teaching on the bed; he should never teach on the bed whereupon he sleeps.тАЩ

  • рдЕрд╕реНрдпрд╛рд░реНрдерд╡рд╛рджрдГ рд╕реНрд░рд╡рддреНрдпреН рдЕрдиреНреРрдХреГрддрдореН ред рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рд░рдореНрднреЗ рдЕрдиреНреРрдХреГрддрдВ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдо рд╕реНрд░рд╡рддрд┐ ред рдУрдорд╛ рдХреГрддрдВ13 реРрд╢рдмреНрджреЗрди рд╕рдВрд╕реНрдХреГрддрдореН ред рд╕рд╛рдзрдирдВ рдХреГрддреЗрддрд┐ рд╕рдорд╛рд╕рдГ ред рдЕрде рд╡рд╛ реРрдХреГрдд14 рдЙрдЪреНрдЪрд╛рд░рд┐рддреЛ рдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордгрд┐ рддрджреН реРрдХреГрддрдВ рд╕реБрдЦрд╛рджрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рдкрд░рдирд┐рдкрд╛рддрдГ ред рдкрд░рд╕реНрддрд╛рдЪреН рдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддреМ ред рдЪрдХрд╛рд░реЗрдгрд╛рдиреНреРрдХреГрддрдореН рдЗрддрд┐ рд╕рдВрдмрдзреНрдпрддреЗ ред рд╕реНрд░рд╡рддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рд╢реАрд░реНрдпрддрд┐ рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЙрднрд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдореН рдЕрдкрд┐ рдиреИрд╖реНрдлрд▓реНрдпрдореН рдЕрдзреНрдпрдпрдирд╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдкрд╛рджреНрдпрддреЗ ред рдЕрдзреАрддрдВ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдо рдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рдХрд░реНрдордгрд┐ рд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреБрдЬреНрдпреЗрдд рддрдиреН рдирд┐рд╖реНрдлрд▓рдВ рднрд╡рддреАрддрд┐ рдирд┐рдиреНрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╡рд╛рджрд╢реН рдЪ ред рдкрд╛рдХрд╛рд░реНрдердВ рдирд┐рд╖рд┐рдХреНрддрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрдкрд╛рдХрдХреНрд╖реАрд░рд╛рджреЗрд░реН рдЕрд╡рдЪреНрдЫрд┐рджреНрд░рд┐рддреЗ рднрд╛рдЬрдиреЗ рдп рдЗрддрд╕реН рддрддреЛ рд╡рд┐рдХреНрд╖реЗрдкрдГ рдкреНрд░рдХреНрд╖рд░рдгрдВ рддрддреН рд╕реНрд░рд╡рддреАрддреНрдпреН рдЙрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рд▓рдмреНрдзрдкрд╛рдХрд╕реНрдп15 рдкрд┐рдгреНрдбреАрднреВрддрд╕реНрдп рднреЛрдЧреНрдпрддрд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд╕реНрдп рдпреЛ рд╡рд┐рдирд╛рд╢рдГ рд╕ рд╡рд┐рд╢рд░рдгрдореН рее реи.ренрек рее
рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

Here also, in accordance with what has gone before (under 71), тАШone should pronounce the Praс╣Зava in the beginning and at the end of the VedaтАЩ;тАФwhich means that the syllable is to be pronounced in the beginning and at the end of the action of reading the Veda.

The term тАШpraс╣ЗavaтАЩ stands for the syllabic тАШoс╣ГтАЩ; as is clear from what the text adds later onтАФтАШnot accompanied by the syllable oс╣Г.тАЩ

тАШAlwaysтАЩтАФhas been added in order to show that the rule applies to every act of study. Without this term it would appear, from the context, that it applies to only that first study by the Religious Student which is done for the getting up of the text. When the adverb тАШalwaysтАЩ has been added, it becomes clear that the rule applies to all forms of studying,тАФthat which is done for the purpose of keeping the memory of the text fresh, or that which is done by the Householder and other people in obedience to the injunction that тАШthe Veda should be studied every day.тАЩ As regards the reciting of Vedic mantras during the Twilight Prayer, etc., the use of the syllable тАШoс╣ГтАЩ the author is going to enjoin directly (in Verse 78). What is laid down here is not meant to be a necessary accompaniment of the Veda,тАФwhich would mean that the rule is to be followed whenever one pronounces any Vedic passage; thus it is that the Praс╣Зava is not used with Vedic mantras on the following occasions: at oblations poured into fire, or during the japa of mantras, or in course of the teaching of scriptures, or at the recitation of the тАШY─Бjy─БтАЩ and other hymns, or when Vedic passages are quoted only by way of illustration. From all this it follows that the adverb тАШalwaysтАЩ is meant to show only that the rule laid down applies to that study of the Veda which forms the subject-matter of the context. As for the necessity of using the Praс╣Зava at the beginning of oneтАЩs daily study, this is secured by the construing of the term тАШalwaysтАЩ of the preceding verse with the present one.

In praise of what has been enjoined the text addsтАФтАШIf it is not accompanied by the syllable oс╣Б, etc.тАЩ If, in the beginning, the Veda is not accompanied by the syllable тАШoс╣Г,тАЩ it trickles off. The compound тАШanoс╣Еkс╣ЫtamтАЩ is to be expounded as тАШthat which is not accompanied,тАФi.e., sanctifiedтАФby the syllable oс╣ГтАЩ according to P─Бс╣Зini, 2. 1. 32; or, it may be expounded as тАШthat Veda in which the syllable oс╣Б is not uttered,тАЩтАФthe order of the terms in this case being in accordance with the rule laid down in connection with the тАШSukh─БdiтАЩ group, according to P─Бс╣Зini, 6. 2. 170.

тАШAt the endтАЩтАФat the close. The particle тАШandтАЩ indicates that the term тАШnot accompanied by the syllable omтАЩ is to be construed here also.

тАШTrickles off-тАФbecomes shattered.тАЩтАФBoth these terms are meant to indicate the futility of the study. The sense being that that religious act, in which the Veda studied in the said defective fashion is used, absolutely fails to accomplish its purpose. This is an Arthav─Бda meant to be deprecatory of the said method of study. When milk is placed in a pot, the milks passes off all round; and this is what is called тАШtrickling offтАЩ; and if the milk becomes destroyed after it has been boiled and become solidified, this is what is called тАШbecoming shattered.тАЩтАФ(74)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

тАШVi┼Ы─лryati тАЩтАФavasthitim na labhate, тАШdoes not obtain any standingтАЩ (Kull┼лka);тАФтАШbecomes absolutely uselessтАЩ (Medh─Бtithi);тАФтАШis not understoodтАЩ (Govindar─Бja and N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa),

This verse is quoted in Madanap─Бrij─Бta (p. 99);тАФin Vidh─Бnap─Бrij─Бta (p. 521);тАФand in Smс╣Ыticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 136) in support of the view that the Praс╣Зava should he pronounced at the close of the reading also.

Apastamba-Dharmas┼лtra, 4. 13. 16.тАФтАШThe syllable Om is the gate of Heaven; therefore when going to read the Veda, one should begin with it.тАЩ

074 Let him always pronounce the syllable Om at the beginning and at the end of (a lesson in) the Veda; (for) unless the syllable Om precede (the lesson) will slip away (from him), and unless it follow it will fade away.

  • рдкрд╡рд┐рддреНрд░реИрд░реН рджрд░реНрднреИрд░реН рдПрд╡ рдкрд╛рд╡рд┐рддрдГ16 рд╢реБрдЪрд┐рддреНрд╡рдореН рдЖрдкрд╛рджрд┐рддрдГ ред рдЕрдШрдорд░реНрд╖рдгрд╛рджрд┐рд╕реН рддреБ17 рдордиреНрддреНрд░реЛ рдиреЗрд╣ рдкрд╡рд┐рддреНрд░рд╢рдмреНрджреЗрдиреЛрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ, рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордЪрд╛рд░рд┐рдгрд╕реН рддрджрд╛рдиреАрдореН рдЕрдирдзреАрддрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рддреЗрд╖рд╛рдореН ред рди рдЪ рджрд░реНрднрд╛рдГ рд╕реНрд╡рд╕рддреНрддрд╛рдорд╛рддреНрд░реЗрдг рдХрд╛рдВрдЪрд┐рддреН рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдореН рдЕрдХреБрд░реНрд╡рддрдГ рдкрд╛рд╡рдиреЗ рдХрд░рдгрдВ рднрд╡рдиреНрддреАрддрд┐ ред рдЕрд╡рд╛рдиреНрддрд░рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкрд╛рд░рд╛рдкреЗрдХреНрд╖рдпрд╛ рд╕реНрдореГрддреНрдпрдиреНрддрд░реЗ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгреЛрдкрд╕реНрдкрд░реНрд╢рдирдВ рдкреНрд░рддреАрдпрддреЗ ред рдЖрд╣ рдЪ рдЧреМрддрдордГ- “рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгреЛрдкрд╕реНрдкрд░реНрд╢рдирдВ рджрд░реНрднреИрдГ ред рдкреНрд░рд╛рдХреНрдХреВрд▓реЗрд╖реНрд╡реН рдЖрд╕рдирдВ рдЪ” (рдЧреНрдзреН рез.рекрео, релреж) ред

  • рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдпрд╛рдореИрд╕реН рддреНрд░рд┐рднрд┐рдГ рдкреВрддрдГ ред рдореБрдЦрдирд╛рд╕рд┐рдХрд╛рд╕рдВрдЪрд╛рд░реА рд╡рд╛рдпреБрдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╕реН рддрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рдореЛ рдирд┐рд░реЛрдзрдГ рд╢рд░реАрд░реЗ рдзрд╛рд░рдгрдВрдореН,рдмрд╣рд┐рд░реН рдирд┐рд╖реНрдХреНрд░рдордгрдирд┐рд╖реЗрдзрдГ, рддрд╕реНрдп рд╕реНрдореГрддреНрдпрдиреНрддрд░реЗ рдзрд░рдгрдХрд╛рд▓рд╕реНрдп рдорд╛рдирдВ рд╕рдорд╛рдореНрдирд╛рддрдореН ред рдордиреНрддреНрд░рд╛рдиреБрд╕реНрдорд░рдгрдВ рдЪ ред

  • рдирдиреБ рдПрд╡рдореН рдЗрддрд░реЗрддрд░рд╛рд╢реНрд░рдпрдГ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рджреН рдЕрдХреГрддреЗрд╖реБ18 рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдпрд╛рдореЗрд╖реБ реРрдХрд╛рд░реЛ рди рдХрд░реНрддрд╡реНрдпрдГ, рди рдЪреНреРрдХрд╛рд░реЗрдг рд╡рд┐рдирд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдпрд╛рдореЛ рдирд┐рд╡рд░реНрддрддреЗ ред рдиреИрд╖ рджреЛрд╖рдГ ред “рддреНрд░рд┐рд░реН рдЬрдкреЗрддреН” рдЗрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдпрд╛рдореЗрд╖реБ рдорд╛рдирд╕рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкрд╛рд░реЗрдгреНреРрдХрд╛рд░рд╕реНрдп рд╕реНрдорд░рдгрдореН рдЙрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рди рд╣рд┐ рдирд┐рд░реБрджреНрдзрдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╕реНрдп рд╢рдмреНрджреЛрдЪреНрдЪрд░рдгрдВ рд╕рдВрднрд╡рддрд┐ ред рдпрджреНрдпреН рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЬрдкрдГ рдХрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рджреН рд╡рд╛рдЧреНрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкрд╛рд░рд╕рд╛рдзреНрдпреЛ рднрд╡рддрд┐ ред рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдзреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рдзреНрдпрдпрдиреЗ рддреБ рдкреБрдирд░реН рдЙрдЪреНрдЪрд╛рд░рдгрдВ рд╡рд┐рд╡рдХреНрд╖рд┐рддрдореН ред рдЕрдзреНрдпрдпрдирдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдпрд╛ рдПрд╡рдВрд░реВрдкрддреНрд╡рд╛рдЪреН рдЫрдмреНрджрдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рд╣реНрдпреН рдЕрдпрдВ19 рдзрд╛рддреБрдГ, рд╢реНрд░реЛрддреНрд░рдЧреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдпрд╢реН рдЪ рд╢рдмреНрджреЛ рди рдХреЗрд╡рд▓реЗрди рдордирд╕рд╛ рдЧреГрд╣реНрдпрддреЗ ред
  • рди рдЪрд╛рдпрдореН реРрдХрд╛рд░рдзрд░реНрдореЛ рдпреЗрдирд╛рдиреНрдпрддреНрд░рд╛рдкрд┐ рддрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрдиреН рдЙрдЪреНрдЪрд╛рд░реНрдпрдорд╛рдгреЗ рд╜рдкрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╕рдЬреНрдпреЗрдд ред рдЙрдХреНрддрдВ рдЪ “рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдзреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рд░рдореНрднреЗ рдХрд░реНрддрд╡реНрдпрдГ” рдЗрддрд┐ ред реРрдХрд╛рд░рдзрд░реНрдорддреНрд╡реЗ рд╣рд┐ рд▓реМрдХрд┐рдХреЗрд╖реБ рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпреЗрд╖реНрд╡реН рдУрдореН рдЗрддрд┐ рдмреНрд░реВрдо рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рд╖реБ рдкреНрд░рд╕рдЬреНрдпреЗрдд ред рдЧреМрддрдореЗрди рддреБ рдкрдард┐рддрдореН- “рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдпрд╛рдорд╛рд╕реН рддреНрд░рдпрдГ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрджрд╢ рдорд╛рддреНрд░рд╛рдГ” рдЗрддрд┐ (рдЧреНрдзреН рез.рекреп) ред рдорд╛рддреНрд░рд╛рд╢рдмреНрджреЗрди рдЪрд╛рд╡рд┐рдХреГрддрд╕реНрдп рд╕реНрд╡рд░рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдХрд╛рд░рд╛рджреЗрд░реН рдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдиреН рдХрд╛рд▓рдГ рд╕ рдЙрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рддрддреНрд░ рд╡рд┐рд░реЛрдзрд╛рддреН рд╕реНрдореГрддреНрдпрдиреНрддрд░реЛрдХреНрддрдГ рдХрд╛рд▓реЛ рдирд╛рд╕реНрддрд┐, рди рдЪ рдордиреНрддреНрд░рд╕реНрдорд░рдгрдВ рддрддреНрд░рд╛рдиреНреРрдХрд╛рд░рд╛ рдЕрдкрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдпрд╛рдорд╛рдГ рд╕рдиреНрддреАрддрд┐ рдиреЗрддрд░реЗрддрд░рд╛рд╢реНрд░рдпрджреЛрд╖рд╛рдкрддреНрддрд┐рдГ ред рддрдд реРрдХрд╛рд░рдореН рдЕрд░реНрд╣рддрд┐ рдХрд░реНрддреБрдореН рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢реЗрд╖рдГ ред рдпрджрд╛рдпрдВ рд╕рдореБрджрд╛рдп рдПрд╡ рд░реВрдврд┐рд░реВрдкреЗрдг рдкреНрд░рдгрд╡рд╡рдЪрдирдГ ред рдпрджрд╛ рддреБ рдХрд░рдгрдВ рдХрд╛рд░рдГ ред рдУрдореН рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдПрддрд╕реНрдп рдХрд╛рд░ рдЙрдЪреНрдЪрд╛рд░рдгрдореН реРрдХрд╛рд░рд╕реН рддрджрд╛ рдирд╛рд╕реНрддрд┐ рдкрджрд╛рдиреНрддрд░рд╛рдкреЗрдХреНрд╖рд╛ ред рдкреНрд░рдгрд╡рд╢рдмреНрджреЗрди рдХрд░реНрддрд╡реНрдпрддрд╛рдореН рдЙрдХреНрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреНрд░реНреРрдХрд╛рд░рдореН рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЕрдиреБрд╡рджрддреНрдпреН рдЕрдд рдПрддрд╛рд╡реН рдПрдХрд╛рд░реНрдереМ ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪ рджрд░реНрд╢рд┐рддрдореН рее реи.ренрел рее
рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

The term тАШk┼лс╣нaтАЩ means тАШku┼Ыa-bladeтАЩ;тАФтАШSeated uponтАЩ them,тАФi.e., seated upon ku┼Ыa-blades pointing eastwards. The accusative ending in тАШk┼лс╣н─БnтАЩ being in accordance with P─Бniс╣Зi 1. 4. 46, тАШadhisth─лnsth─Бs─Бm karma,тАЩ where the latter part consists of the factors тАШath─БтАЩтАФтАШ─БтАЩтАФтАШ─Бs─Бm.тАЩ In the word тАШparyup─Бs─лnaс╕етАЩ also we have an тАШ─БтАЩ, the word containing the factors тАШpariтАЩтАФтАШupaтАЩтАФтАШ─БтАЩтАФтАШ─Бs─лnaс╕етАЩ; the prefixes тАШpariтАЩ and тАШupaтАЩ having no significance at all.

тАШSanctified by ku┼Ыa-bladesтАЩ;тАФi.e., having been made pure. The term тАШpavitraтАЩ cannot stand for the Aghamarс╣гaс╣Зa and other mantras; for the simple reason that at the time that the text is being dealt with, the student has not read those mantras. Nor are ku┼Ыa-blades capable, by their mere presence, to bring about purification for one who does no (purificatory) act; thus then, the necessity of some intervening act being essential, we are led to conclude, on the basis of another Smс╣Ыti, that this act is in the form of touching the sense-organs; Gautama (1.48-50) having prescribed тАШthe touching of the organs with Ku┼Ыa-blades and seating upon Ku┼Ыa-blades pointing eastwards.тАЩ

тАШPurified by means of three Breath-suspensionsтАЩтАФThe air passing through the mouth and the nostrils is called тАШpr─Бс╣Зa,тАЩ тАШbreathтАЩ; and the тАШ─Бy─БmaтАЩ of this is its suspension, holding within the body, preventing its going out. Another Smс╣Ыti (Y─Бj├▒avalkya, ─Аc─Бra, 23) has laid down the measure of the time during which the breath is to be suspendedтАФas also the mantra accompanying it,тАФтАЬOne, witholding his breath, should mutter three times the G─Бyatr─л along with the Praс╣Зava and the ┼Ъiras,тАФthis is what is called тАШBreath-suspensionтАЩ.тАЭ The revered Va┼Ыiс╣гс╣нha has added to these the Great Vy─Бhс╣Ыtis also. It is the end of the mantra that should mark the end of the suspension, no other limit for it being prescribed. In as much as all Smс╣Ыtis are meant to serve the same purpose, we must accept this same method of тАШBreath-suspensionтАЩ to be meant by the present text also, specially as there is no inconsistency with it.

Objection.тАФтАЬWhat has been said here involves a mutual interdependence: until the Breath-suspensions have been performed one should not pronounce тАШOс╣Г,тАЩ while without this syllable тАШOс╣ГтАЩ there can be no тАШBreath-suspensionтАЩ.тАЭ

There is nothing wrong in this. When Y─Бj├▒avalkya lays down that тАШone should mutter three times; etc.,тАЩ all that is meant is the mental act of remembering, thinking of, the syllable тАШOс╣ГтАЩ; for when the breath is suspended, there can be no utterance of any syllable; though it is true that тАШJapa,тАЩ тАШReciting,тАЩ is (in most cases) something that can be accomplished only by an operation of speech. In connection with the reading of the Veda however, what is intended is actual utterance of the syllable; and this for the simple reason that the act of reading consists of actual utteranceтАФthe root (in тАШadhyayanaтАЩ) signify ing the waking of sound, and sound is that which is heard by the Ear, and not that which is cognised only by the mind.

What is prescribed here is not something applicable to the syllable тАШOс╣ГтАЩ itself,тАФwhereby it could be made applicable to the uttering of the syllable on other occasions also. It has been said that the syllable should be pronounced at the beginning of Vedic study; but if the. rule here laid down were meant to be applicable to all utterances of the syllable, it would have to be observed in connection with such utterances of it in ordinary parlance as when one says тАШwe say yes (oс╣Г).тАЩ

Then again, Gautama (l.49) has declared that. тАШthe three Breath-suspensions extend over fifteen moments.тАЩ The term тАШm─Бtr─Б,тАЩ тАШmoment,тАЩ stands for that point of time which is taken up in the pronouncing of a simple unmodified vowel; and in as much as this cannot be consistent with the time-limit prescribed by Y─Бj├▒avalkya, this latter cannot be accepted as applicable to what is prescribed by Gautama; in which connection again no mantras are laid down. From this it is clear that there can be тАШBreath-suspensionsтАЩ even without the uttering of the syllable тАШoс╣Г.тАЩ And thus there need be no mutual interdependence.

Then alone does the man тАШbecome entitled to the syllable oс╣ГтАЩ;тАФi.e., to the тАШpronouncingтАЩ of the syllable,тАФthe word тАШpronouncingтАЩ having to be supplied if the entire term тАШoс╣Еk─БraтАЩ is taken as standing for the Praс╣Зava. If however we take the term тАШk─БrтАЩ separately in the sense of making,тАФso that тАШoс╣Бk─БraтАЩ means the making or uttering of the syllable тАШoс╣Г,тАЩтАФthen we do not need to supply any other word. The uttering of the syllable having been laid down (under 74), where it is called тАШpraс╣ЗavaтАЩ;тАФthe term тАШoс╣Еk─БraтАЩ in the present sense simply serves the purpose of explaining what that тАШpraс╣ЗavaтАЩ is.

So that тАШpraс╣ЗavaтАЩ and тАШoс╣Еk─БraтАЩ are synonymous terms; as we have already pointed out (in the Bh─Бс╣гya on 74).тАФ(75)

тАШPavitraiс╕етАЩтАФтАШKu┼Ыa-bladesтАФby which the seat of the vital airs is touchedтАЩтАФ(Medh─Бtithi);тАФтАШThe Aghamarс╣гaс╣ЗaтАЩ and other Vedic texts (noted by Medh─Бtithi, but rejected by him, though adopted by Nandana). Burnell has translated the term as тАШgrass-rings on the third fingerтАЩ;тАФthis is in exact conformity with the present usage, where a blade of Ku┼Ыa, twisted into the form of a ring, is worn on the third finger on the occasion of all religious ceremonies.

This verse is quoted in Vidh─Бnap─Бrij─Бta (p. 521);тАФin V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 522), which explains тАШpr─Бkk┼лl─БnтАЩ as pr─Бgagr─Бn тАШpointing eastwardsтАЩ,тАФand тАШpavitraiс╕етАЩ simply as тАШp─Бranaiс╕етАЩ тАШpurificatoriesтАЩ;тАФin Saс╣Гsk─Бramay┼лkha (p. 49), which explains тАШpr─Бkk┼лl─БnтАЩ as тАШwith tips pointing towards the eastтАЩ;тАФin Saс╣Гsk─Бraratnam─Бl─Б (p. 316) which has the same explanations and adds that it refers to Ku┼Ыa-blades;тАФin Smс╣Ыticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 135) which has the same explanation and explains тАШpavitraiс╕етАЩ as purificatory;тАФalso in Nс╣Ыsiс╣Гhapras─Бda (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 471).

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рддреБрд▓реНрдп-рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐

Gautama-Dharmas┼лtra, 1.51-56.тАФтАШThe sense-organs should be touched with Ku┼Ыa-blades;тАФthere should be three Breath-suspensions, of fifteen units; and the seat should be on Ku┼Ыa-grass pointing eastwards.тАЩ

Baudh─Бyana-Dharmas┼лtra, 2.4.5,7.тАФтАШAt the commencement of the performance of all acts, as also before the Twilight Prayers, one should sprinkle himself with the sanctifying blades and thereby prepare himself;тАФto this effect it is declared that seated on Ku┼Ыa-blades, holding Ku┼Ыa-blades in the hand, sprinkling himself with water, one should repeat the G─Бyatr─л a thousand times;тАФbeing purified with three Breath-suspensions.тАЩ

K┼лrmapur─Бс╣Зa (V─лramitrodaya-─Аhnika, p. 254).тАФтАШSeated on Ku┼Ыa-blades pointing eastwards, with mind collected, he should perform throe Breath-suspensions and then the Twilight Prayers.тАЩ

This verse is a valedictory supplement to the foregoing injunction.

тАШOut of the three VedasтАЩтАФfrom the three Vedas.

тАШMilkedтАЩтАФchurned out; just as butter is churned out of the curd.

рдЕрдпрдВ “рддрддреН рд╕рд╡рд┐рддреБрд░реН рд╡рд░реЗрдгреНрдпрдореН” (рд░реНрд╡реН рей.ремреи.резреж) рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдПрддрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдГ рдЧрд╛рдпрддреНрд░реНрдпрд╛рдГ рдЙрддреНрдкрддреНрддреНрдпрд░реНрдереНрд╡рд╛рджреЛ рд╡рд┐рдзрд╛рдирд╛рд░реНрдердГ ред рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╢реНрд▓реЛрдХреЗ рдЪрд╛рд░реНрдерд╡рд╛рджрд╛рджреН рдПрд╡ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рд╣реГрддреАрдирд╛рдореН рдЕрдкрд┐ рд╡рд┐рдзрд╛рдирдореН ред рдХреНрд░рдорд╕реН рддреБ рдкрд╛рдард╛рд╡рдЧрдореНрдпрдГ ред рд╡рдХреНрд╖реНрдпрддрд┐ рдЪ-

  • рдПрддрджреН рдЕрдХреНрд╖рд░рдореН рдПрддрд╛рдВ рдЪ рдЬрдкрдиреН рд╡реНрдпрд╛рд╣реГрддрд┐рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд┐рдХрд╛рдореН ред рдЗрддрд┐ ред (рдореНрдзреН реи.ренрео)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

The present verse is a valedictory description of the origin of the G─Бyatr─л -verse beginning with the words тАШtat savitur vareс╣Зyam,тАЩ which serves the purpose of introducing the coming injunction. As for the injunction of the Vy─Бhс╣Ыtis, this is to be deduced from the valedictory description contained in the preceding verse. As for the actual order in which the several syllables have to be pronounced, that is ascertained from the order in which they are found mentioned in tho text. The author is also going to lay down in the next verseтАФтАШThey should pronounce this syllable (om), and this verse (тАШtat savitur, etc.тАЩ), preceded by the Vy─Бhс╣Ыtis.тАЩ

тАШMilkedтАЩтАФchurned out.

тАЬBeginning with тАШtatтАЩ;тАЭтАФthough this being all that the text says, it might refer to an altogether different verseтАФтАШtat savitur vс╣Ыс╣Зimahe, etc.тАЩ (с╣Ъgveda, 5. 82. 1), which is not three-footed,тАФyet it is the three-footed verse that should he taken as referred to here; and it is the тАШS─Бvitr─лтАЩ verse that is three-footed.

In as much as Ka┼Ыyapa and other sagos are also called тАШPraj─Бpati,тАЩ the text has added the qualification тАШSupremeтАЩ; so that it is Hiraс╣Зyagarbha that becomes specified; as it is He who dwells on, the highest spot, from where there is no reversion (to worldliness).

This has been added with a view to show the extreme importance of the S─Бvitr─л verse;тАФit was churned by the highest of all Praj─Бpatis, out of the Vedas.тАФ(77)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

HopkinsтАФтАЬThis verse is one of the most famous in literature, Whitney has discussed it in Vol. I., pp. 111-112 of the new edition of ColebrookтАЩs Essays. His translation runs as followsтАФтАШOf Savitar, the heavenly, that longed-for glory may we win, and may himself inspire our prayers.тАЩ

This verse is quoted in Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava (Pr─Бya┼Ыcitta, p. 52), as supporting the view that the g─Бyatr─лmantra, is тАШborn of the VedaтАЩ par excellence-,тАФalso in V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 338).

рдПрддрд╛рдВ рдЪ “рддрддреН рд╕рд╡рд┐рддреБрд░реН рд╡рд░реЗрдгреНрдпрдореН” рдЗрддрд┐ рд╕рд╛рд╡рд┐рддреНрд░реАрдореН ред рд╡реНрдпрд╛рд╣реГрддрдпрдГ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╛ рдпрд╕реНрдпрд╛рд╕реН рддрд╛рдореН рд╡реНрдпрд╛рд╣реГрддрд┐рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд┐рдХрд╛рдВ ред рддрд┐рд╕реНрд░рдГ рдкреНрд░рдХреГрддрд╛ рдПрд╡ рддрд╛ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рд╣реГрддрдпреЛ рдЧреГрд╣реНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ, рдкреНрд░рдХреГрддрдкрд░рддреНрд╡рд╛рджреН рдЕрд╕реНрдп, рди рд╕рдкреНрдд рд╕рддреНрдпрд╛рдиреНрддрд╛рдГ рее реи.ренрео рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

Though this verse is syntactically connected with the section dealing with the Injunction of Vedic study, yet it is to be taken as embodying the injunction of recitation during the Twilight-Prayers; and as regards the тАШG─Бyatr─лтАЩ-verse itself, the mention of it (in the present verse) is merely for the purposes of reference (the injunction of its recitation having already gone before), while that of the Praс╣Зava and the Vy─Бhс╣Ыtis forms the direct injunction of the recitation of these, which has not been enjoined anywhere else.

To this some people make the following objection:тАФ

тАЬThis cannot be regarded as an Injunction pertaining to the Twilight Prayers; as these do not form the subject-matter of the present context. Even if it was an injunction, it could only be one pertaining to the Religious Student; as it is the Student whose duties are being propounded in the present context. But this is not possible, since the text has added the qualification тАШlearned in the VedaтАЩ; and certainly the student just initiated could never be тАШlearned in the Veda.тАЩ Further, the text also adds a particular fruitтАФтАШbecomes endowed with Vedic meritтАЩ; while the Injunction of the Twilight-Prayers is a compulsory one. Then again, we do not understand what is this fruit, called тАШVedic meritтАЩ which is described as proceeding from the recitation. If what is meant is the merit proceeding from the recitation of the Veda, and if the attaining of this merit is what is meant by being тАШendowed with Vedic meritтАЩтАФthen, in regard to this view it has to be noted that so far as the Injunction of Veda-reciting is concernedтАФwhich forms the subject-matter of the present context,тАФthere can be no other result proceeding from it, except the understanding of the meaning of tho Vedic texts; for the simple reason that no such result has been anywhere mentioned. Further, in as much as there is a perceptible result in the shape of the comprehension of meaning, there can be no room for the assuming of any other results. The injunction of Veda-reciting that there is for the Householder and others,тАФin the words тАШday after day one should recite the VedaтАЩтАФthis also is a compulsory one; and the results mentioned in connection with it, in the shape of тАШmilk, and honey, etc.,тАЩ this is only a valedictory supplement. From all this it is clear that the present verse cannot be regarded as an Injunction (of recitation during the Twilight Prayers). Specially as, if it were taken as an Injunction, all the above difficulties will have to be explained. On the other band, if the verse be taken as a valedictory reference, then the term тАШrecitingтАЩ could be taken as referring to the Reciting of the Veda, which forms the subject-matter of the context; and in that case it would be possible to construe the term тАШVedic meritтАЩ also in some way or the other.тАЭ

Our answer to the above is as follows:тАФ

It has been already explained that the implications of context are always set aside by those of Syntactical Connection; and for the very reason that the terms тАШlearned in the VedaтАЩ and тАШTwilight prayersтАЩ are not connected with the subject-matter of the context,тАФthe present Injunction is to be taken as pertaining to something else. The Injunction is simply to the effect that during the two Twilight Prayers one should pronounce the three expressions (OmтАФS─Бvitr─л verseтАФVy─Бhс╣Ыtis); and the term тАШlearned in the VedaтАЩ is merely descriptive?

тАЬBut as a matter of fact, it is possible only for persons in the Householder and other stages to be тАШlearned in the VedaтАЩ; the Student can never be so.

What has this possibility got to do with the matter? If the term is taken as merely descriptive of what is already known from other sources, then the injunction contained in the verse becomes applicable to people in all stages of life. While if the term тАШlearned in the VedaтАЩ were taken as a significant epithet of the Nominative agent (of the act enjoined), then the student would not be entitled to the act.

тАЬWhy should the term be taken as merely descriptive?тАЭ

For the simple reason that there would (otherwise) be a syntactical split. The injunction pertaining to the Injunction of the Twilight Prayers, what has to be enjoined regarding it is the reciting of the Praс╣Зava and the Vy─Бhс╣Ыtis, which has not been enjoined anywhere else, Now, if in addition to these, something else were taken as enjoined,тАФin the form of тАШbeing learned in the Veda,тАЩтАФthen there would be a syntactical split [the sentence in question containing two injunctions, (a) тАШshould recite the Praс╣Зava, etc.,тАЩ and (b) тАШshould learn the VedaтАЩ]; and it is not legitimate to enjoin (by means of a single sentence) several details pertaining to an act already enjoined. Nor is it possible (as another alternative) to take the mention of the Praс╣Зava and the Vy─Бhс╣Ыtis as merely descriptive [because their injunction has not been met with anywhere else].

From all this it follows that what the Text means is as follows:тАФтАШIn connection with the reciting of the G─Бyatr─л that has been enjoined in relation to the Twilight Prayers, there is this further detail that the said recitation is to lie preceded by the uttering of the Praс╣Зava and the Vy─Бhс╣Ыtis.тАЩ

The mention of the тАШBr─Бhmaс╣Зa’ is only by way of illustration.

It has been argued above thatтАФтАЬthe text speaks of a result, while the Injunction of the Twilight Prayers is a compulsory one.тАЭ

But what inconsistency is there in this? While what is enjoined is a compulsory act, the result mentioned may follow from the further detail mentioned in the text; the meaning being that тАШthe said result follows from the previously enjoined Twilight Prayer, when it is accompanied by the recitation of the Praс╣Зava and the Vy─Бhс╣Ыtis. Just as when the ordinary Agnihotra is performed with the water brought over in the milking vessel, there comes about the particular result in the shape of cattle; and this in (?) accordance with the injunction that тАШfor one desiring cattle water should be brought in the milking vessel.тАЩ

It is on the strength of this last injunction that we have made bold to say what we have said above. In reality the injunction contained in the verse is not an optional one at all (meant only for those desiring the particular result mentioned). Specially as another Smс╣Ыti (Y─Бj├▒avalkya,

    1. clearly lays it down as a compulsory injunctionтАФтАШOne should recite the G─Бyatr─л along with the ┼Ъiras, preceded by the Vy─Бhс╣Ыtis.тАЩ

Further, you have yourself argued that the exact nature of the result (тАШVedic meritтАЩ) cannot be ascertained (which is an argument against the text being taken as laying down a result). As a matter of fact, what тАШVedic meritтАЩ means is as follows:тАФтАШThe merit that has been described in the Veda as resulting from the saying of the Twilight Prayers accrues to man only when he recites all the three expressionsтАФand not by reciting the G─Бyatr─л only.тАЩ тАШPuс╣Зya,тАЩ тАШmerit,тАЩ is excellence. Since Smс╣Ыtis are based upon the Veda, what is mentioned in the Smс╣Ыtis is also called тАШVeda-merit,тАЩ which last expression stands for the тАШmerit of the Veda.тАЩ

тАЬWhat is the merit of the Veda?тАЭ

That (merit) which is expounded by the Veda. The merit that results from the Veda being recited may also be called тАШthe merit of the VedaтАЩ; but by virtue of the specific relationship, it is what is expounded by the Veda,тАФand what is produced by itтАФthat should be spoken of as тАШmerit of the Veda.тАЩ As for the producing of merit, this is done by other things also, such as sacrificial performances and the like; while the expounding of it is done by the Veda only.

Some people have taken the last foot of the Verse to mean as followsтАФтАЬWhat has been enjoined as compulsory Vedic Study becomes fulfilled merely by reciting the three expressions during the Twilight Prayers.тАЭ

But this is not right. For if the present text meant this, then it would be providing an option to what has been laid down as the compulsory тАШVedic StudyтАЩ; and this would mean the partial rejection of this study. But so long as we can avoid it, it is not right to admit the rejection of any injunction.

тАШThis syllableтАЩтАФrefers to the syllable тАШoс╣Г.тАЩ

тАЬBut this is not a single letter, containing as it does, two or three syllables.тАЭ

Our answer is that the term тАШsyllableтАЩ here stands for тАШvowel-soundтАЩ and тАШcontact with consonants.тАЩ Hence the term denotes that which forms the subject-matter of the context.

тАШThis VerseтАЩтАФi.e., the S─Бvitr─л verse тАШtat saviturvareс╣Зyam, etc.тАЩ

тАШPreceded by the Vy─Бhс╣Ыtis;тАЩтАФi.e., that before which the Vy─Бhс╣Ыtis have been uttered. Here only the three Vy─Бhс╣Ыtis are meant,тАФthese alone having been mentioned in the present context (in verse 76),тАФand not the seven, ending with тАШSatyam.тАЩ

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

Medh─Бtithi (P.111,1.11)тАФPr─Бpte hi karmaс╣Зi, &c.тАЩтАФThis is a paraphrase of Kum─БrilaтАЩs dictumтАФ

pr─Бpte karmaс╣Зi n─Бneko vidh─Бtuс╣Г ┼Ыakyate guс╣Зaс╕е |
apr─Бpte tu vidh─лyante vahavo’pyekapatnataс╕е |

This verse is quoted in Apar─Бrka (p. 50), which explains тАШetadakс╣гaramтАЩ as the Praс╣Зava;тАФand in Nity─Бch─Бrapaddhati, (p. 189).

  • рдирдиреБ рдЪрд╛рднреНрдпрд╕реНрдпреЗрддреНрдпреН рдЕрдиреЗрдирд╛рдкрд┐ рди рдХрд╛рдЪрд┐рджреН рд╡рд┐рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрд╛ рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпреЛрдкрд╛рддреНрддрд╛ ред рд╕рддреНрдпрдореН ред рдЬрдкрдГ рдкреНрд░рдХреГрддрд╕реН рддрдореН рдЕрднреНрдпрд╕реНрдпреЗрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рддреАрдпрддреЗ ред рдЖрд╡реГрддреНрддрд┐рдГ рдкреМрдирдГрдкреБрдгреНрдпреЗрди рд╕реЗрд╡рд╛ ред

  • рдорд╣рддреЛ рд╜рдкреНрдпреН рдПрдирд╕рдГ ред рдорд╣рддреН рдкрд╛рдкрдВ рдЪ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдорд╣рддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐ ред рддрддреЛ рд╜рдкрд┐ рдореБрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ, рдХрд┐рдВ рдкреБрдирд░реН рдЙрдкрдкрд╛рддрдХреЗрднреНрдпрдГ ред рдЕрдкрд┐рдГ рд╕рдВрднрд╛рд╡рдиреЗ, рди рд╕рдореБрдЪреНрдЪрдпреЗ ред рднреЗрджреЛрдкрд╛рджрд╛рдиреЗрди рд╕рдореБрдЪреНрдЪрдпрд╛рд╡рдЧрдореЛ рдпрдерд╛ рджреЗрд╡рджрддреНрддрд╕реНрдпрд╛рддреНрд░ рдкреНрд░рднреБрддреНрд╡рдВ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрджрддреНрддрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдкрд┐ ред рдЗрд╣ рди рддрдерд╛ рдирд┐рд░реНрджреЗрд╢рдГ ред

  • рдЕрддреНрд░реЛрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рд╡рд┐рдзрд┐рд░реН рдПрд╡рд╛рдпрдореН ред рдкрд╛рдкрдкреНрд░рдореЛрдЪрдирд╛рд░реНрде рдПрд╡рд╛рдпрдВ рдкреНрд░рдпреЛрдЧрдГ ред рдпрддреН рддреВрдХреНрддрдВ “рд╡рд┐рд╖рдорд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреИрд░реН рд╡рд┐рдХрд▓реНрдкреЛ рди рд╕рд┐рдзреНрдпрддрд┐” рдЗрддрд┐ рдЬрдкрдкреНрд░рд╛рдпрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рддреНрдд рдПрд╡рд╛рд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рд╡рд┐рдХрд▓реНрдкрд╛рд░реНрдереЛ рднрд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдпрддрд┐ ред рдЕрдШрдорд░реНрд╖рдгрд╛рджрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдкрд╛рдкрд╛рдкрдиреЛрджрдирдореН рдЙрдХреНрддрдореН, рддреЗрдирд╛рд╕реНрдп рд╡рд┐рдХрд▓реНрдкрдГ ред рдЕрдШрдорд░реНрд╖рдгреЗ рд╣рд┐ рддреНрд░реНрдпрд╣рдореН рдЙрдкрд╡рд╛рд╕ рдЙрдХреНрддрдГ ред рдЗрд╣рд╛рд╢реНрдирдиреНрдиреН рдПрд╡ рдорд╛рд╕рд┐рдХреЗрди рдкреНрд░рдпреЛрдЧреЗрдг рд╢реБрдзреНрдпрддрд┐ ред рддрддреЛ рди рджреВрд░рд╡рд┐рдкреНрд░рдХреГрд╖реНрдЯреЗрди рддрдкрд╕рд╛ рдкреНрд░рдореАрдпрддреЗ, рдпреЗрди рд╡рд┐рд╖рдорд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрддрд╛ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рддреН ред

  • рдЕрде рд╡рд╛ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдХреГрддрд╕реНрдпреИрдирд╕рдГ рд╢реБрджреНрдзрд┐рд░реН рдПрд╖рд╛ рдЧреНрд░рд╣рд╛рджреМрд╕реНрдерд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рд╕реВрдЪрд┐рддреЗ рджреИрд╡реЗ рджреЛрд╖реЗ ред рддрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рдореЛрдХреНрд╖рдГ ред рдЕрдирд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдореН рдПрди рдЙрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рддрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рдореБрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рддрддреНрдлрд▓реЗрди рди рд╕рдВрдмрдзреНрдпрдд рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЕрд░реНрдердГ ред

  • рддреНрд╡рдЪреЗрд╡рд╣рд┐рдГ ред рдЬреАрд░реНрдгрдпрд╛ рддреНрд╡рдЪрд╛ рдореБрдХреНрддрдГ рд╕рд░реНрдкреЛ рдпрдерд╛ рднрд╡рддрд┐ ред рдирд┐рд░рд╡рд╢реЗрд╖реЗрдг рдкрд╛рдкрдирд╛рд╢ рдПрддреЗрди рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдкрд╛рджреНрдпрддреЗ ред рдпрддреН рддреБ рджреМрд╢реНрдЪрд░реНрдорд╛рджрд┐рд╕реВрдЪрд┐рддрдВ30 рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдХреГрддрдореН рдЕрд╢реБрднрдВ рддрддреНрд░ рд╕реНрдореГрддреНрдпрдиреНрддрд░реЗ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдпрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рддреНрддрдореН рдЖрдореНрдирд╛рддрдВ рдмрд╣реБ ред рддрддреН рдкреНрд░рд╛рдпрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рддреНрддреЗрд╖реНрд╡реН рдПрд╡ рдирд┐рджрд░реНрд╢рдпрд┐рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдордГ ред рдПрддрджреН рдПрд╡рд╛рднрд┐рдкреНрд░реЗрддреНрдпреЛрдХреНрддрдореН ред

  • рдЬрдкрддрд╛рдВ рдЬреБрд╣реНрд╡рддрд╛рдВ рдЪреИрд╡ рд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдкрд╛рддреЛ рди рджреГрд╢реНрдпрддреЗ ред (рдореНрдзреН рек.резрекрем) рдЗрддрд┐ рее реи.ренрепрее
рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

The term тАШbahiс╕е,тАЩ тАШin open air,тАЩ stands for uncovered spot; the sense being that it should be done outside towns and villages, on the bank of rivers and such places.

тАШA thousand times, repeatingтАЩтАФreciting it again and again.

тАЬThe affix тАШkс╣ЫtvasuchтАЩ (in the term тАШSahasrakс╣Ыtvaс╕етАЩ) also signifies repetition, which is again denoted by the word тАШabhyasyaтАЩ also; so there is needless repetition.тАЭ

The repetition is not objectionable, in view of a distinction between general and particular. That is to say, the word тАШabhyasyaтАЩ denotes repetition in general, and when the question arises as to the particular number of repetitions, we have the text adding тАШa thousand times.тАЩ Both the general and the particular could not be regarded as signified by the single word ending with the тАШkс╣ЫtvasuchтАЩ affix; because this latter word always stands in need of a particular act (that has to be done a thousand times). The mere expression тАШdevadattaс╕е pan chakritvoтАЩhaс╕е,тАЩ тАШDevadatta five times during the dayтАЩ does not signify anything until the word тАШbhuс╣Еkte,тАЩ тАШEats,тАЩ is added.

тАЬBut the term тАШrepeatingтАЩ also does not signify any particular act.тАЭ

True; but the act of reciting forms the subject-matter of the context; so that the repeating is understood as pertaining to that act; тАШrepetitionтАЩ standing for attending to it again and again.

тАШEven from great sinтАЩ;тАФhe becomes freed from even such heinous sins as тАШBr─Бhmaс╣Зa-killingтАЩ and the like; what to say of minor offences?

тАШApi,тАЩ тАШEven,тАЩ denotes possibility, not cumulation; cumulation is expressed when more things than one are mentioned separately; as in the sentenceтАФтАШthere is sovereignty of Devadatta, and of Yaj├▒adatta also.тАЩ There is no such separate mention in the text.

QuestionтАФтАЬFrom what minor offences does the man become freed? Cow-killing and such acts have been regarded as тАШminor offencesтАЩ; and for every one of these the scriptures have prescribed distinct expiatory rites along with all their details. While as regards those acts that are not done consciously, but which are regarded as must have been done,тАФthough no definite expiation could be prescribed for them, yet they would be got rid of by means of the Twilight Prayers and such other compulsory rites prescribed for daily performance. Then again, if what is mentioned in the present verse were a real expiation, it should have come under the section on Expiatory Rites (Ch. XI); just as it is said (under 11. 77)тАФтАШOne may recite the text of the Veda while keeping due restraint over food.тАЩ Further, if the present verse were meant to prescribe an expiatory rite, the whole section dealing with Expiatory Rites (Ch. XI) would he superfluous. For, what accused person would omit to do the expiation consisting of the mere reciting of mantras, and go in for the very difficult rites endangering the body and very life itself? Says an old sayingтАФтАШIf honey were available in a place within easy reach, wherefore should one go to the hills? The desired end having been accomplished, which wise man could put forth further efforts?тАЩтАФand againтАФтАШWhat can he obtained for a single coin, no wise man purchases for ten coins.тАЩ Nor can the verse be taken as a valedictory supplement to what forms the subject-matter of the context (i.e., Vedic Study), because there is no ground for connecting it syntactically with the context,тАФsuch grounds, for instance, as being found defective if taken apart from the context and so forth.тАЭ

Our answer to the above is as follows:тАФThe present verse is a direct Injunction; and the act laid down is done for the removing of sins. It has been argued thatтАФтАЬWhat is laid down here (being too easy) could not be regarded as optional with those rites that are prescribed in a different context and are very much more difficult.тАЭ But it can certainly be taken as optional with those expiations which consist in Mantra-recitations. For instance, the reciting of the Mantra has been declared as destroying all sins; and with this what is laid down in the present verse could be taken as optional. In connection with the Aghamarс╣гaс╣Зa-Mantra, three days fasting is prescribed, while according to what is laid down in the present verse, the man becomes freed by doing th e reciting for a month, but taking two ordinary meals every day. Thus the difference between the two is not so great as to lead us to regard them as very diverse in character.

Or, what is mentioned here may be taken as purifying the man from such past sins as arc indicated by the evil position of planets, etc.; and it is from these sins that the man becomes free. тАШSinтАЩ is something undesirable; from this the man becomes freed,тАФi.e., is not affected by the results of those sins.

тАШJust as the snake from the slough,тАЩтАФjust as the snake becomes freed from the cast-off skin. This means that the sin is completely removed.

For such past sins as are indicated by the discolouring of the skin and such other diseases, other Smс╣Ыtis have prescribed many expiatory rites. All this we shall explain under the section on Expiatory Rites.

It is in view of what, is said in the present verse that we have the sayingтАФтАШThere is no fall for people who go on reciting mantras and pouring libations.тАЩтАФ(79)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

тАШVahiс╕етАЩтАФBurnell represents Medh─Бtithi as explaining this term to be тАШon a river-island and the like.тАЩ This is not right; the word used by Medh─Бtithi is тАШnad─лpulin─БdauтАЩтАФwhich means тАШon the bank of rivers and such placesтАЩ.

This verse is quoted in Apar─Бrka (p. 1220) where тАШvahiс╕етАЩ is explained as тАШoutside the villageтАЩтАФand тАШtrikamтАЩ as тАШthe S─Бvitr─л along with the Vy─Бhс╣ЫtisтАЩ;тАФand in Gad─Бdharapaddhai (K─Бlas─Бra, p. 30), which explains тАШtrikamтАЩ as (1) Praс╣Зava. (2) Vy─Бhс╣Ыti and (3) G─Бyatr─л.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рддреБрд▓реНрдп-рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐

**(Verses 78-79)
**

See Comparative notes for [Verse 2.78].

B├╝hler

079 A twice-born man who (daily) repeats those three one thousand times outside (the village), will be freed after a month even from great guilt, as a snake from its slough.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШBy this verseтАЩтАФby the S─Бvitr─л.

тАШBereftтАЩ;тАФhe who fails to observe the Twilight Prayers and neglects Vedic Study.

тАШOdiumтАЩтАФBlame.

тАШAmong good menтАЩтАФAmong the highly cultured people.

тАШIncursтАЩтАФbecomes open to.

With a view to show what sort of odium he incurs, the Text addsтАФтАШand of the timely performance of his own duty.тАЩтАФтАШTimelyтАЩтАФe.g., the sixteenth year for the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa and so forth. When the man is bereft of these rites, he becomes despised.

From this it is clear that even though the boy may have been initiated, and as such become qualified for Vedic Study,тАФyet, if he is bereft of the S─Бvitr─л, he becomes a тАШVr─Бtya,тАЩ apostate.

What is meant by тАШhis own dutyтАЩ is just that duty which is common to the three castes; and this is the duty of Initiation. It is only when we interpret it thus that the qualification тАШtimelyтАЩ comes to have any sense. If the тАШdutyтАЩ meant were the duties of Vedic Study and the rest, the text would have said simply тАШperformance of his own dutyтАЩ (without the qualification тАШtimelyтАЩ).

The term тАШyoniтАЩ being synonymous with тАШbirthтАЩ denotes caste. So what is meant is the person of the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa and other castes.

The present verse is only a descriptive supplement, added for the purpose of making the Expiatory Rites prescribed for the Vr─Бtya (apostate) applicable to the omissions mentioned here.тАФ(80)

реРрдХрд╛рд░рдГ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реЛ рдпрд╛рд╕рд╛рдВ рддрд╛ реРрдХрд╛рд░рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд┐рдХрд╛рдГ ред рдорд╣рд╛рд╡реНрдпрд╛рд╣реГрддрдпрдГ рдкреНрд░рдХреГрддрд╛ рдПрд╡ рднреВрд░реН рднреБрд╡рдГ рд╕реНрд╡рд░реН рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдПрддреЗ рд╢рдмреНрджрд╛ рдЕрднрд┐рдзреАрдпрдиреНрддреЗ ред рдЕрд╡реНрдпрдпрд╛ рдЕрд╡рд┐рдирд╛рд╢рд┐рдиреНрдпрдГ ред рдлрд▓рд╕реНрдп рджреАрд░реНрдШрдХрд╛рд▓рддреНрд╡рд╛рджреН рдПрд╡рдореН рдЙрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рдЕрдиреНрдпрдерд╛ “рд╕рд░реНрд╡ рдПрд╡ рд╢рдмреНрджрд╛ рдирд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рдГ” рдЗрддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рдгрдореН рдЕрдирд░реНрдердХрдореН ред рддреНрд░рд┐рдкрджрд╛ “рддрддреН рд╕рд╡рд┐рддреБрд░реН” рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдПрд╖рд╛ рд╕рд╛рд╡рд┐рддреНрд░реА рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордгреЛ рдореБрдЦрдореН ред рдЖрджреНрдпрддреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдореБрдЦрд╡реНрдпрдкрджреЗрд╢рдГ рдЕрддрд╢реН рдЪрд╛рд░рдореНрднреЗ рдЕрдзреНрдпреЗрдпрдореН рдПрддрджреН рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЕрд╕реНрдпреИрд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерд╡рд╛рджрдГ ред рдЕрде рд╡рд╛ рдореБрдЦрдВ рджреНрд╡рд╛рд░рдореН рдЙрдкрд╛рдпреЛ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд┐рд░реН рдЕрдиреЗрди рднрд╡рддреАрддреНрдпреН рдПрддрджреН рдПрд╡рд╛рд╣ рее реи.реорез рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАЬPreceded by the syllable Oс╣ГтАЭтАФin the beginning of which the syllable тАШOс╣ГтАЩ occurs.тАФтАШMah─Бvy─Бhс╣ЫtisтАЩ;тАФthis refers to the three syllables тАШbh┼лс╕етАФbhuvaс╕етАФsvaс╕е,тАЩ which form the subject-matter of the present context.

тАШImperishableтАЩ;тАФthe syllables are so called in view of the fact that the results proceeding from their repetition are longstanding. If this were not meant, then the qualification would be superfluous, as all words are equally imperishable, eternal.

Three-footed S─Бvitr─л;тАФthe verse тАШtat savituс╕е, etc.тАЩ

тАШThe mouth of Brahman.тАЩтАФThese are called тАШmouthтАЩ in the sense that they form its opening. Hence this verse is to be regarded as the valedictory supplement of the Injunction that these should be recited at the beginning of Vedic Study.

Or тАШmouthтАЩ may mean portal, the means;тАФthe sense being that union with Brahman is reached by this means. This is what is described in the next verse.тАФ(81)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

тАШBrahmaс╣Зo mukhamтАФтАЬLiterally, the mouth of Brahman is meant to convey the double sense (of leading to, and leading to union with, Brahman). Both interpretations are given by Medh─Бtithi, Kull┼лka. and R─Бghav─Бnanda; while Govindar─Бja, N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa and Nandana explain it merely as the beginning or portal of the Veda.тАЭтАФBuhler.

This verse is quoted in Madanap─Бrij─Бta (p. 71) as defining the тАШBrahmamukhaтАЩ, which has been declared by N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa to be the formula for the ─Аcamana;тАФin V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 522), as laying down the beginning of study;тАФin the same work again (─Аhnika, p. 253), where it is explained as meaning that the name тАШsandhy─БтАЩ (Twilight Prayers) is applied to all those acts that are performed with the formula herein specified;тАФalso on p. 321, along with the next three verses.

This first line of this verse is quoted in Apar─Бrka, (p. 1290).

The verse is quoted in Saс╣Гsk─Бramay┼лkha (p. 50), which explains тАШtisraс╕етАЩ as тАШBh┼лс╕е-bhuvaс╕е-svaс╕етАЩ and тАШbrahmaс╣Зo mukhamтАЩ as тАШto be pronounced at the beginning of Vedic readingтАФand in Smс╣Ыticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 135), which notesтАФтАШom bh┼лrbhuvaс╕еsvaс╕етАЩ are the three Vy─Бhс╣Ыtis,тАФtatsavituс╕е &c., is the S─Бvitr─л; all this forms the тАШmukhaтАЩ, i.e. beginning, of тАШBrahmanтАЩ, i.e. the Veda.

**(verses 81-82)

─Аpastamba (Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava, p. 284).тАФтАШSeated upon ku┼Ыa, holding ku┼Ыa and water in his hand, facing the East, one shall repeat the G─Бyatr─л a thousand times, or a hundred times, or without any limit.тАЩ

Yogi- Y─Бj├▒avalkya (Do., 283).тАФтАШThe Religious Student and the Agnihotrin should repeat the G─Бyatr─л 108 times: the Hermit and the Renunciate, more than 1,000 times,

Yama (Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava, p. 286).тАФтАШThere is nothing superior to the G─Бyatr─л for purposes of Japa; there is no penance higher than the G─Бyatr─л; there is no meditation higher than the G─Бyatr─л; there is no Homa higher than the Viс╣гс╣Зusmс╣Ыti, 55. 15-16тАФ[reproduces the words of Manu].

Yama (V─лramitrodaya-Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 429).тАФтАШHe who acquires the three Vy─Бhс╣Ыtis preceded by the syllable om, and the S─Бvitr─л, Brahmacharya and is called ┼Ъrotriya.тАЩ

Laug─Бkс╣гi (Do.).тАФтАШHaving pronounced om bh┼лrbhuvaс╕еsvaс╕е, he pronounces the S─Бvitr─л verse beginning with Tat savituс╕е.тАЩ

тАШBaudh─Бyana-Dharmas┼лtra, 2. 4. 21.тАФтАШThe Br─Бhmaс╣Зa who daily, at all junctures, meditates upon this, becomes purified to Brahmaс╣Зa and merged in Br─Бhmaс╣З; following the scriptures, he wins the Brahmic regions.тАЩ

Vy─Бsa (Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava, p. 285).тАФтАШBy repeating the G─Бyatr─л ten times one becomes absolved from all little sins committed during the day; repeated a hundred times, she destroys a host of sins; repeated a thousand times, she destroys all minor sins; by repeating it a lakh of times, all the most heinous sins are destroyed; by repeating it a crore of times, one obtains all that is desired.тАЩ

Saс╣Гvarta (V─лramitrodaya-Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 522).тАФтАШOne should utter the Praс╣Зava first: after that, the Vy─Бhс╣Ыtis; and then the S─Бvitr─л.тАЩ

Yogi-Y─Бmavalkya (V─лramitrodaya-─Аhnika, p. 258).тАФтАШG─Бvatr─л is Brahm─Б and S─Бvitr─л is Rudra.тАЩ

Yama (V─лramitrodaya-─Аhnika, p. 321, also Par─Б┼Ыaramadhava, p. 284).тАФтАШOne should daily repeat the G─Бyatr─л, which is destructive of all sins, a thousand times, or a hundred times, or at least ten times; the Lord put the G─Бyatr─л in one pan and the Vedas along with the subsidiary sciences in the other pan of the scale; and the two were found equal.тАЩ

Aс╣Еgiras (V─лramitrodaya-─Аhnika, p. 322)тАФтАШOne who is intent upon the Praс╣Зava, the seven Vy─Бhс╣Ыtis, and the three-footed G─Бyatr─л has no fear anywhere.тАЩ

H─Бr─лta (V─лramitrodaya-─Аhnika, p. 323).тАФтАШThe Praс╣Зava, the Vy─Бhс╣Ыtis the S─Бvitr─л verse,тАФthese constitute the S─Бvitra, whereby one becomes absolved from sins; by hundred repetitions, from sins of thought; by thousand repetitions, from sins of word; and by ten thousand repetitions, from all sins, and has his soul perfectly pure.тАЩ

He who, untired, recites this, day after day, for three years, turns into air, and becoming transfigured into ─Аk─Б┼Ыa, reaches the supreme brahman.тАФ(82)

рдЖрдХрд╛рд╢ рдЗрд╡ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреА рд╡рд┐рднреБрдГ рд╕рдВрдкрджреНрдпрддреЗ, рдЦрдореВрд░реНрддрд┐рдГ рдЦрд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡рд╡рд╛рдиреН рднрд╡рддрд┐ ред рди рддреБ рдореВрд░реНрддрд┐рдГ рд╢рд░реАрд░рдореН, рдЖрдХрд╛рд╢рд╕реНрдп рд╢рд░реАрд░рд╛рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рддреН ред рдЕрде рдХрд┐рдореН рдЗрджрдВ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдо, рдпрджреН рд░реВрдкрд╛рдкрддреНрддрд┐рд░реН рдЙрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛рдирдиреНрджрд░реВрдкрдГ, рдпрд╕реНрдпреЗрдореЗ рдХреНрд╖реЗрддреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдГ рдкрд╡рдирдЬрд╡реЛрджреНрдзрддрд╕реНрдп рд╡рд╛рд░рд┐рд░рд╛рд╢реЗрд░реН рдЗрд╡реЛрд░реНрдордпрдГ ред рддреЗ рдпрдерд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╢рд╛рдиреНрддрд╛рд╡рд╕реНрдереЗ рддрд╕реНрдорд┐рдВрд╕реН рддрджреНрд░реВрдкрд╛ рднрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ ред рдПрд╡рдореН рдЕрдореА рддрджреНрд░реВрдкрд╛ рдЖрддреНрдорд╛рдирдГ рд╕рдВрдкрджреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ ред рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рддрд╢реН рдЪ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдореН рдПрддрджреН рджреНрд╡рд╛рджрд╢реЗ рд╡рдХреНрд╖реНрдпрддреЗ ред рдЕрдзреНрдпрдпрдирдореН рдЗрджрдВ рдЧрд╛рдпрддреНрд░реНрдпрд╛рд╢реН рдЪреЛрджрд┐рддрдВ рди рдЬрдкреЛ, рди рдЪрд╛рд╡реГрддреНрддрд┐рдЧрдгрдирд╛рд╕реНрддрд┐ ред рдЕрддрдиреНрджреНрд░рд┐рдд рдЗрддрд┐рд╡рдЪрдирд╛рджреН рдмрд╣реБрдХреГрддреНрд╡рдГ рдХрд░рдгрдВ рдкреНрд░рддреАрдпрддреЗ ред рд╕рдХреГрддреНрдкреНрд░рдпреЛрдЧреЗ рд╣рд┐ рдирд╛рд╕реНрддрд┐ рддрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рд╢рдЩреНрдХрд╛ ред рдореЛрдХреНрд╖рд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рдиреЛ рд╜рдпрдВ рд╡рд┐рдзрд┐рдГ рее реи.реореи рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

He becomes omnipresent, all-pervading, like ─Аk─Б┼Ыa.

тАШTransfigured into ─Аk─Б┼ЫaтАЩтАФmeans that he acquires the nature of ─Аk─Б┼Ыa. тАШM┼лrti,тАЩ тАШFigure,тАЩ does not stand here for the Body; as ─Аk─Б┼Ыa has no тАШbodyтАЩ at all.

тАЬWhat is this тАШBrahmanтАЩ into whose form the man is said to become merged?тАЭ

It is the Supreme Soul, of the nature of Bliss; He of whom all these embodied souls are mere inodes, just as waves are of the ocean perturbed by the force of wind. And just as when the ocean becomes calm, the waves become merged into it, in the same manner the embodied souls become transformed and merged into the Supreme Soul. All this is going to be described in detail in Discourse 12.

What is enjoined in the present context is the mere reciting and study of the G─Бyatr─л verse, not its Japa, repetition; this is shown by the fact that the number of repetitions is not stated.

тАШUntiredтАЩ;тАФthis denotes that the recitation is to be carried out again and again; as a single recitation can never tire a person.

What is enjoined here pertains to persons seeking for Final Release.тАФ(82)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

This verse is quoted in V─лramitrodaya (─Ас╕еnika, p. 321), which supplies the following explanatory notes:тАФ

тАШV─Бyubh┼лtaс╕етАЩтАФas quick- moving as the wind, or тАШencased in the Subtle BodyтАЩтАФas explained in Kalpataru;тАФтАШKham┼лrtim─БnтАЩтАФbecoming as all-pervading as the ─Аk─Б┼Ыa, becomes the Supreme Self.,

It is quoted also in Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava (─Аc─Бra, p. 286) as eulogising the japa of the G─Бyatr─л mantra;тАФand in Saс╣Гsk─Бraratnam─Бl─Б (p. 236).

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рддреБрд▓реНрдп-рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐

The mono-syllable is the highest Brahman; Breath-suspensions are the highest austerity; nothing is higher than the S─Бvitr─л verse; truth is better than Silence.тАФ(83)

рд╕реНрдпреБрдГ” рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЖрдкрд╕реНрддрдореНрдмрд╡рдЪрдирд╛рддреН (рдЖрдкреНрдзреН рез.резрей.реп) ред рдЙрдкрдирд┐рд╖рджреНрднрд╛рд╖реНрдпреЗ рдЪреИрддрджреН рдЕрдиреНрдпрдерд╛ рдЖрдЪрдордирд╡рджреН рд╡рд┐рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреЗрддрд┐рдХрд░реНрддрд╡реНрдпрддрд╛рдХреЗ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрдирд┐рд░реЛрдзреЗ рд╡рд░реНрддрддреЗ ред рдкрд░рдВ рддрдкрдГ рдЪрд╛рдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рдпрдгрд╛рджрд┐рднреНрдпрдГ ред рдХрд┐рдВ рдкреБрдирд╕реН рддрд╕реНрдп рд╢реНрд░реИрд╖реНрдареНрдпрдореН ред рднрдХреНрддрд┐рд░реН рдПрд╖рд╛ ред рд╕рд╛рд╡рд┐рддреНрд░реНрдпрд╛рдГ рдкрд░рдВ рдордиреНрддреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдВ рдирд╛рд╕реНрддрд┐ ред рдПрд╖рд╛рдореН рдЗрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛ ред рдореМрдирд╛рддреН рд╕рддреНрдпрдВ
