рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдпрддреЗ ред рд╕рддреНрдпрд╡рдЪрдиреЗ рд╡рд┐рдзреНрдпрд░реНрдереЛ рд╜рдкрд┐ рддрдерд╛рдиреБрд╖реНрдард┐рддреЛ рднрд╡рддрд┐ ред рдореМрдиреЗ рддреБ рдХреЗрд╡рд▓рдореН рдЕрдиреГрддрдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд╖реЗрдзрд╛рдиреБрд╖реНрдард╛рдирдореН рдПрд╡ ред рдЕрд░реНрдерд╡рд╛рджреЛ рд╜рдпрдВ рд╢реНрд▓реЛрдХрдГ рее реи.реорей рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

The тАШmonosyllableтАЩ is the syllable тАШom.тАЩтАФIt is the тАШSupreme Brahman,тАЩ in the sense that it is the means of reaching Brahman. This assertion is based upon the fact that Brahman is attained by the тАШrepeating,тАЩ and тАШthe meditation upon the signification,тАЩ of the syllable (as mentioned in Yogas┼лtra 1.28). тАШOmтАЩ is a name of Brahman; as says the Yogas┼лtra (1.23)тАФтАШThe Praс╣Зava is expressive of Him (God).тАЩ

тАЬIn comparison with what is this the highest?тАЭ

It is higher than all other forms of Brahman-meditation. The meditation upon the syllable тАШomтАЩ as Brahman is superior to all the several forms of meditation mentioned in such texts as тАШOne should meditate upon food as BrahmanтАЩ (Taittir─лya Upaniс╣гad, 2.2.1), тАШThe teaching is that the Sun is BrahmanтАЩ (Ch─Бndogya Upaniс╣гad, 3.19.1); and this for the simple reason that the attainment of Brahman has been described as proceeding from the mere recitation of that syllable; and also because the word itself has been described as тАШBrahman,тАЩ in such passages asтАФтАШOne who is well versed in Brahman in the form of Word attains the supreme Brahman.тАЩ (Maitry upaniс╣гad, 6.22). Nothing is beyond the reach of words, and of’ all words the syllable тАШomтАЩ is the very source: as says the ┼ЪrutiтАФтАШJust as the needle pierces through all the leaves, so in the same manner is all speech pierced by om, all this is om itselfтАЩ (Ch─Бndogya Upaniс╣гad, 2.23.4). The тАШpiercingтАЩ spoken of in this passage means тАШpervasion,тАЩ тАШbecoming the receptacle.тАЩ тАЬBut in what manner is all speech pierced by om?тАЭ

Well, as regards the word of the Veda, it has already been pointed out (in verse 74) that its source lies in the syllable тАШomтАЩ As regards the words of secular speech, it has been declared by ─Аpastamba (1.4.13.9) that тАШAll sentences should be preceded by om.тАЩ

The above passage (from the Ch─Бndogya) has been explained differently in the Upaniс╣гad-bh─Бс╣гya; we are not reproducing that explanation here, as it has no bearing on the present context.

The term тАШbreath-suspensionтАЩ here stands for the act of suspending the breath along with the entire procedure beginning with the sipping of water.

тАШHighest austerityтАФi.e., an austerity higher than the C─Бndr─Бvaс╣Зa and the rest.

тАЬWhat is the superiority here (meant by the epithet тАШhighestтАЩ)?тАЭ

It is purely figurative.

тАШThere is nothing higher than the S─Бvitr─лтАЩ;тАФi.e., no other mantra.

In praise of all this we have the next expressionтАФтАШTruth is better than silenceтАЩ тАШSilenceтАЩ is control of speech. And the result accruing from the telling of truth is superior to that resulting from the control of speech. Since the telling of truth implies the acting up to a positive injunction, while in silence there is observance of the mere prohibition of telling lies.

This verse is purely valedictory.тАФ(83)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

Medh─Бtithi (P. 114, 1. 12)тАФтАШ─Аpastamba vacan─БtтАЩтАФThis refers to ─АpastambaтАЩs Dharmas┼лtra 1.4.13.9, the whole of which reads as followsтАФ

loke ca bh┼лtikarmasvetad─лnyeca v─Бky─Бni syuryath─Б pupy─Бhaс╣Г svassyс╣Ыddhimiti

This verse is quoted in V─лramitrodaya (─Аhnika, p. 321), where the same verse is attributed to Yama also.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

All acts laid down in the VedaтАФтАШoblationsтАЩ in the form of Agnihotra and the rest,тАФas also тАШsacrificesтАЩ in the form of Jyotiс╣гс╣нoma and the rest,тАФтАШpass awayтАЩ; i.e., either they never bring about their results in their entirety, or even when brought about, those results perish quickly.

тАШThis syllableтАЩтАФтАШomтАЩтАФis to be known as тАШimperishable,тАЩ i.e., bringing about imperishable results; since for one who has become merged into Brahman, there is no return to worldly existence. Thus leading to an imperishable result, the syllable is itself called тАШimperishable.тАЩ One of the two terms тАШakс╣гara,тАЩ one is a noun, which forms the subject of the sentence, while the other, is the predicate, and is taken in its literal sense.

That same syllable is also Brahman, and Praj─Бpati.

This also is purely valedictory.

The expression тАШjuhoti-yajatiтАЩ mentions two verbal roots; and the term тАШkriy─БтАЩ stands for the actions of (oblation) and Y─Бga (sacrifice)тАФas denoted by the two roots. The plural number is due to the multiplicity of the acts. Or, the two verbal roots may be taken as standing for the acts of Homa and Y─Бga themselves, while ’ kriy─БтАЩ stands for the other acts of charity and the like. The whole is a copulative compoundтАФmade up of the three terms тАШjuhoti,тАЩ and тАШkriy─БтАЩтАФthe acts of H oma and Y─Бga being separately mentioned by reason of their importance.

Some people have held that this praise of the syllable тАШomтАЩ by itself (as apart from the and the verse) is meant to enjoin the repetition of the syllable; and they argue that this cannot be taken as merely supplementary to the foregoing injunction of the reciting of the S─Бvitr├о along with тАШom,тАЩ etc., as no reference to this latter is made in the present verse; as there is in the case of the sacrifice, in connection with which we find two passagesтАФ(a) тАШYadaс╣гс╣н─Бkapalo bhavati g─Бyat chainam brahmavarchasena pun─Бti,тАЩ and (b) тАШYannavakapalastс╣Ыvс╣Эtaiv─Бsmimstejo daс╕Нh─Бii,тАЩтАФwhere reference is distinctly made to a foregoing injunction; so that so long as it is found possible (on the basis of this reference) to connect the injunctions syntactically (and treat them as a single injunction), there can be no justification for splitting them up into two distinct injunctions. In the present instance, on the other hand, when it is said that тАШthis should be regarded as imperishable,тАЩ there is no reference to any thing that has gone before; nor is there any reference made to the S─Бvitr─л, etc. Por these reasons, the present text is to be taken as a self-contained injunction, and not as supplementary to something else. Further, the verbal affix in тАШj├▒eyaс╕етАЩ тАШ(should be regarded)тАЩ is purely injunctive. And this, taken along with the word тАШbrahma,тАЩ gives the sense that тАШthis should he regardedтАФi.e., meditated uponтАФas BrahmanтАЩ; and this тАШmeditationтАЩ stands for the mental process of repeating the syllable.тАФ(84)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

тАШKс╣гarantiтАЩтАФтАШPass awayтАФdo not bring about their complete results, or their results disappear quicklyтАЩтАФ(Medh─Бtithi, Govindar─Бja, Kull┼лka and N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa);тАФтАШPerishтАФas far as their form and results are concernedтАЩтАФ(Nandana).

тАШBrahmaтАЩтАФThe neuter form is accepted by Medh─Бtithi, Govindar─Бja, Kull┼лka and R─Бghav─Бnanda. N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa and Nandana read the masculine form тАШbrahm─БтАЩ, and explain the phrase as тАШjust like Brahm─Б, the Praj─Бpati.тАЩ

This verse is quoted in V─лramitrodaya (─Аc─Бra, p. 321), where it is explained thatтАФтАШakс╣гaramтАЩ stands for the syllable тАШomтАЩ,тАФand this is тАШakс╣гaraтАЩ in the sense that its effect in the form Final Release тАШnever perishesтАЩ (na-kс╣гarati);тАФand that the syllable тАШomтАЩ is to be regarded as тАШPraj─БpatiтАЩ on the ground of its being expressive of that deity. Here again this same verse is attributed to Yama also.

Medh─БtithiтАЩs remarks on p. 115,11. 1-8 are based upon M─лm─Бс╣Гs─Б-S┼лtra 1. 4. 17-22.

This verse is quoted in V─лramitrodaya (Paribh─Бс╣г─Б, p. 79), which reads тАШAkс╣гaram ┼Ыreс╣гс╣нhamтАЩ for тАШduс╣гkaram j├▒eyamтАЩ and explains it as тАШBrahma-praс╣Зava.тАЩ

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

The тАШenjoined offeringтАЩ is that which forms the subject of injunctions; such as Jyotiс╣гс╣нoma and the rest; such acts are called тАШenjoined offering,тАЩ as they have been enjoined by words like тАШshould offerтАЩ and the rest, and are performed by means of external acts, and with the full accompaniment of priests and other innumerable details.

The Japa, тАШ Repeating of MantrasтАЩ is not an тАШofferingтАЩ; but with a view to eulogise it, it has been spoken as an тАШofferingтАЩ only figuratively; consequently this cannot be included under the term тАШenjoined offering.тАЩ

This latter тАШexcels,тАЩтАФis a better, superior, offering than the Jyotiс╣гс╣нoma and the rest,тАФтАШten timesтАЩ.

What is meant here is that the Repeating of Mantras is highly efficacious; the meaning being that the results proceeding from the Repetition are the same, but larger, as those proceeding from the Ritualistic Offerings. It is not meant that the Repeating of Mantras actually brings about results larger than those brought about by the ritualistic sacrifices; for if it were really so, who тАШwould ever undertake the performance of the latter, which involve much physical hardship and the expenditure of much wealth? For these reasons it is clear that what is said here is a mere praise (of the Repeating of Mantras); just like the assertion that тАШOne attains all desirable ends by the

Final Oblation.тАЩ All that is meant is that from this act also the same results follow, in the shape of Heaven and the rest; but the difference iu the amount of human effort involved leads to the difference in the degree of the result. And as the text does not specify any particular result, it should be taken to mean that by the Repeating of Mantras one obtains the same resultsтАФin the shape of heaven, landed property, children and cattleтАФas those proceeding from sacrificial performances.

тАШThe Inaudible, a hundred timesтАЩтАФThat repeating of Mantras is called Inaudible which is not heard by any other person, however near he may be.

тАШA thousand timesтАФthe Mental.тАЩтАФThat in which the Mantra in meditated upon by a mere mental operation.

The тАШInaudibleтАЩ and other qualifications pertain to all kinds of Repeating Mantras (and not only to the repeating of the G─Бyatr─л, etc.); the continuity of the context, starting from verse 82, having been broken. Hence, whenever there is repetition of MantrasтАФin the course of either Expiatory Rites, or the rites performed for the allaying of portents, or those intended to bring about prosperity,тАФthe said qualifications become applicable.

The term тАШs─БhasraтАЩ literally means that which has a thousand; and since the noun spoken of is тАШguс╣Зa,тАЩ тАШtimes,тАЩ тАШfold,тАЩ the term means тАШthousand-foldтАЩ; the term тАШfoldтАЩ standing for part. That this refers to the excess of results is clear from the connection of the entire sentence.тАФ(85)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

Medh─Бtithi (P. 115,1. 16)тАФтАШP┼лrс╣Зahuty─Б &c.тАЩтАФSee in this connection S─Бyaс╣Зa-с╣Ъgvedhbh─Бс╣гyaтАФUpodgh─Бta (Introduction).

рдорд╣рд╛рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдГ рдкрд╛рдХрдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╛ рдЙрдЪреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ, рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордпрдЬреНрдЮрдВ рд╡рд░реНрдЬрдпрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛ рдЪрддреНрд╡рд╛рд░реЛ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╛ рднрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ ред рд╡рд┐рдзрд┐рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╛ рдЙрдХреНрддрд╛рд╕реН рддреИрдГ рд╕рдордиреНрд╡рд┐рддрд╛рдГ рд╕рд╣рд┐рддрд╛рдГ ред рдХрд▓рд╛рдореН рдЕрдВрд╢рдВ рд╖реЛрдбрд╢реАрдВ рдирд╛рд░реНрд╣рдиреНрддрд┐ ред рд╖реЛрдбрд╢реЗрди рднрд╛рдЧреЗрди рди рд╕рдорд╛ рднрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ ред рдЕрде рд╡рд╛рд░реНрд╣рддрд┐рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддреНрдпрдЩреНрдЧреЗ рдореВрд▓реНрдпрдкрдгрдиреЗ рд╡рд░реНрддрддреЗ ред рдЕрд░реНрд╣рд╢рдмреНрджрд╛рддреН рддрд┐рдкрдВ рдХреГрддреНрд╡рд╛ рдЕрд░реНрд╣рдиреНрддрд┐ рд░реВрдкрдореН рее реи.реорем рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

The five тАШgreat sacrifices,тАЩ leaving off the are what are meant by the тАШfour cooked offerings.тАЩ

тАШEnjoined sacrificesтАЩтАФthose already described (under the preceding verse); along with these latter, the former (four) тАШare not worth the sixteenth partтАЩтАФi.e., are not equal to the sixteenth part.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

тАШP─Бkayaj├▒─Бс╕етАЩтАФThis term stands for the last four of the five тАШMah─Бyaj├▒aтАЩтАФ

  1. Brahmayaj├▒a (Vedic study),
  2. Devayaj├▒a (the Vai┼Ыvadeva offerings),
  3. Pitс╣Ыyaj├▒a (daily ┼Ъr─Бddha offerings),
  4. Bh┼лtayaj├▒a (Bali offerings)
  5. and Manuс╣гyayaj├▒a (Feeding of guests),

according to Medh─Бtithi, Kull┼лka, N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa and Nandana.

According to Govindar─Бja and R─Бghv─Бnanda, it stands for all ┼Ъrauta and Sm─Бrta offerings.

The main classification of sacrifices is based upon the difference in the substances offered. On this basis they have been classified as under:тАФ

(l) Haviryaj├▒as, also called тАШIс╣гtiтАЩ, consisting in the offering of such substances as milk, butter, rice, barley and other grains;тАФthe principal representatives of this class are (a) the Dar┼Ыap┼лrс╣Зam─Бsa, which is described in detail in the ┼Ъatapatha Br─Бhmaс╣Зa (I and II); and its six ectypesтАФ(b) the Agny─Бdh─Бna, (c) the Agnihotra (d) the ─Аgrah─Бyaс╣Зeс╣гс╣нi (e) the C─Бturm─Бsya, (f) the Pa┼Ыubandha and (g) the Sautr─Бmaс╣Зi; all these are offered into fire specially consecrated by the Agny─Бdh─Бna rite, which serving as it does only the purpose of preparing the fire for other sacrifices, is not a sacrifice in the strict sense of the term,тАФas has been remarked by Karka in his commentary on K─Бty─БyanaтАЩs ┼Ъrautas┼лtra.

(2) P─Бkayaj├▒as consisting of the offering of cooked substances, not in the consecrated fire, but in the domestic fire and other receptacles. The seven principal sacrifices included under this category areтАФthe five тАШgreat sacrificesтАЩ (described in ┼Ъatapatha Br─Бhmaс╣Зa 10-5.7 and in Manu, 3.70), the Aс╣гс╣нak─Бs, the P─Бrvaс╣Зa offerings, the ┼Ъr─Бvaс╣З─л, the ─Аgrah─Бyaс╣З─л, the Caitr─л and the ─А┼Ыv─Бyuj─л. These are described in the Gс╣ЫhyaтАФnot ┼ЪrautaтАФS┼лtras. Though the substances offered in these are not very different from those in the Iс╣гс╣нis on Haviryaj├▒as, yet they are classed separately, on the ground that the receptacle of the offerings in their case is not the consecrated fire.

(3) Somayaj├▒as in which the substance offered is the Soma-juice; it includes the following seven sacrificesтАФ(a) Agniс╣гс╣нoma, (b) Atyagniс╣гс╣нoma, (c) Ukthya, (d) ┼Ъoс╕Нa┼Ыin (e) V─Бjapeya, (f) Atir─Бtra and (g) ─Аptoryam─Б. Almost all Somayaj├▒as involve the killing of an animal, hence the Animal-sacrifices, Pa┼Ыuy─Бgas, have been included by older writers under this category; though later writers have drawn a distinction between the Somay─Бga and the Pa┼Ыuy─Бga. The very elaborate sacrifices, such as the A┼Ыvamedha, the R─Бjas┼лya, the Pauс╣Зс╕Нar─лka and the Gosava (according to Devala)тАФare generally classed apart, under the generic name of Mah─Бyaj├▒akratuтАЩ.

(See in this connection, Pr─Бbh─Бkara-M─лm─Бс╣Гs─Б, pp. 251-253).

  • рдХреБрд░реНрдпрд╛рджреН рдЕрдиреНрдпрджреН рдЕрдирд┐рддреНрдпрдВ39 рдЬреНрдпреЛрддрд┐рд╖реНрдЯреЛрдорд╛рджрд┐ ред рдЕрде рд╡рд╛ рддрджреН рдЕрдкрд┐ рди рдХреБрд░реНрдпрд╛рджреН рдпрддреЛ рдореИрддреНрд░реЛ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордг рдЙрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рдорд┐рддреНрд░рдореН рдПрд╡ рдореИрддреНрд░рдореН ред рд╕рд░реНрд╡рднреВрддрдореИрддреНрд░реАрд░рддреЗрди рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгреЗрди рднрд╡рд┐рддрд╡реНрдпрдореН ред рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд╖реНреРрдЗрдпрдкрд╢реБрд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рдЪ рдХреБрддреЛ рдореИрддреНрд░реА ред рдЕрдпрдореН рдЕрд░реНрдерд╡рд╛рджреН рдПрд╡, рди рдкреБрдирдГ рдкрд╢реНрд╡рдЩреНрдЧрдХрд░реНрдордкреНрд░рддрд┐рд╖реЗрдзрдГ, рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╢реЗрд╖рддреНрд╡рд╛рд╡рдЧрддреЗрдГ ред рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдХреНрд╖рд╢реНрд░реБрддрд┐рд╡рд┐рд╣рд┐рддрддреНрд╡рд╛рдЪреН рдЪ рддреЗрд╖рд╛рдореН ред рдЕрддрд┐рдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддреЛ рдЬрдкрд╡рд┐рдзрд┐рдГ рее реи.реорео рее
рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

By means of repeating Mantras alone the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa succeeds;тАФi.e., acquires all desirable results,and also attains Brahman.

No such doubt on this point should be entertained in the mind, asтАФтАЬHow can one acquire, by means of Mantra-repetition alone, such results as are obtained only by means of such elaborate acts as the Jyotiс╣гс╣нoma and the rest, which cost much effort, or from deep and prolonged meditations?тАЭтАФBecause as a matter of fact, such success does actually follow.

тАШHe may do anything else.тАЩтАФIn the shape of the Jyotiс╣гс╣нoma and other non-com pulsory acts, тАФтАШor not do it.тАЩтАФFor тАШone comes to be called a Brahmaс╣Зa if lie is of a friendly disposition.тАЩ тАШMaitraтАЩ is the same as тАШmitra.тАЩ The Brahmaс╣Зa should be friendly to all living beings; and how can there be any friendliness (benevolence) in such acts as the killing of animals during the Agn─лс╣гom─лya offerings?

This passage is purely valedictory; it is not a prohibition of the killing of animals during sacrifices; because it is only supplementary to what has gone before (and as such it cannot be taken as an independent prohibition), and because such killing is directly enjoined in the Veda itself.

Thus ends the process of Repeating Mantras.тАФ(87)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

тАШMaitraс╕етАЩтАФтАШof friendly disposition (towards all living beings)тАЩтАФMedh─Бtithi;тАФтАШworshipper of Mitra, SunтАЩ (suggested by R─Бghav─Бс╣Зanda).

тАШBr─Бhmaс╣Зaс╕етАЩтАФтАШone who will be absorbed in BrahmanтАЩ (Kull┼лka);тАФтАШthe best of Br─Бhmaс╣ЗasтАЩ (R─Бghav─Бnanda);тАФ

Buhler remarksтАФтАЬMedh─Бtithi and Govindar─Бja take the last clause differently: it is declared (in the Veda that) a Br─Бhmaс╣Зa (shall be) a friend (of all creatures).тАЭ But in Medh─Бtithi we find no mention of the Veda here.

The verse is clearly meant to be deprecatory of Animal-sacrifices, which involve the killing of animals, whereas the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa should be friendly to all creatures.

This verse is quoted in Yatidharmasaс╣Гgraha (p. 127).

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рддреБрд▓реНрдп-рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐

Viс╣гс╣Зu-smс╣Ыti, 55.21 and Vasiс╣гс╣нha, 26.12тАФ[reproduce the words of Manu].

B├╝hler

087 But, undoubtedly, a Brahmana reaches the highest goal by muttering prayers only; (whether) he perform other (rites) or neglect them, he who befriends (all creatures) is declared (to be) a (true) Brahmana.
